The Conjunction Waw: Connector vs Circumstantial
Defines waw as connector vs circumstantial with case studies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between waw as a sentence connector ('atf al-jumlah) and waw as a circumstantial clause (hal) and apply that distinction to derive differing Hanafi rulings.

Core Idea
The conjunction waw is ambiguous: it either connects independent sentences or creates a condition; the ruling changes entirely.

In Arabic legal utterances, the simple conjunction waw can carry two distinct functions. It may merely connect two independent sentences without affecting their individual rulings, or it may introduce a circumstantial clause that conditions the main action. This lesson explores that distinction through two examples from Hanafi fiqh and examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over the interpretation of waw in a divorce-related statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two functions of waw
Recognize that waw can be either a sentence connector ('atf al-jumlah) where each clause stands alone, or a circumstantial particle (hal) that makes the second clause a condition for the first.
The passage defines both uses explicitly.
2
Analyze the first example
When a man says 'This woman is divorced thrice, and this woman is divorced,' the waw is a connector. The second woman receives only one divorce because the clauses are independent.
Partnership in the predicate (being divorced thrice) is not obligatory.
3
Analyze the second example
When a woman says 'Divorce me and you have one thousand dirhams,' the interpretation of waw determines the legal outcome.
Abu Hanifa treats it as a connector; the Sahibayn treat it as circumstantial.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds waw as 'atf al-jumlah, so the divorce is without compensation (default in divorce). The Sahibayn hold waw as hal, so the thousand dirhams become a condition and obligatory substitute.
The opposing dalil is that waw indicates a circumstantial state.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, the husband gets nothing; according to the Sahibayn, he is entitled to the thousand dirhams.
This illustrates how grammatical analysis directly impacts fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وقد تكون لعطف الجملة فلا تجب به المشاركة في الخبر كقوله هذه طالق ثلاثا وهذه طالق فتطلق الثانية واحدة فقط وكذا فى قولها طلقني ولك الف درهم حتى اذا طلقها لا يجب شئ للزوج وقالا انها للحال فيصير شرطاً وبدلا فيجب الالف . کبھی واو عطف جملہ کیلئے بھی ہوتی ہے تو اس وقت مشارکت فی الخبر ضروری نہیں ہو گی مثلا اگر کسی نے کہا کہ هذه طالق ثلاثاً و هذه طالق تو دوسری عورت کو صرف ایک طلاق واقع ہو جائیگی اسی طرح اگر کسی عورت نے اپنے شوہر کو طلقني ولك الف در هم کہا تو اگر شوہر نے طلاق دیدی تو اس کو ہزار درہم نہیں ملے گا کیونکہ یہاں واو عطف کیلئے ہے حال کیلئے نہیں ہے اور طلاق میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ بغیر مال کے ہو ۔ اس مقام پر حضرات صاحبین رحمہما اللہ کا اختلاف ہے اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ واو حال کیلئے ہے لہذا یہ طلاق دینے کی شرط ہو گی گویا عورت نے یوں کہا کہ طلقني والحال أن لك الف درهم لہذا اس پر ہزار واجب ہو جائیں گے۔
His statement: And [waw] may be for connecting sentences, so partnership in the predicate is not obligatory, such as his statement: 'This woman is divorced thrice, and this woman is divorced' – then the second woman receives only one divorce. Similarly in her statement: 'Divorce me and you have one thousand dirhams' – if he divorces her, nothing is owed to the husband. But [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said that it is for the circumstantial state, so it becomes a condition and a substitute, so the thousand becomes obligatory. Sometimes waw is for connecting sentences, so at that time partnership in the predicate is not necessary. For example, if someone said, 'This woman is divorced thrice, and this woman is divorced,' then the second woman receives only one divorce. Similarly, if a woman said to her husband, 'Divorce me and you have one thousand dirhams,' then if the husband divorced her, he will not get the thousand dirhams, because here waw is for conjunction, not for the circumstantial state, and the principle in divorce is that it is without compensation. At this point, there is a difference of opinion of the two companions (Sahibayn). The two companions say that waw is for the circumstantial state, so it becomes a condition for divorce; as if the woman said, 'Divorce me while you have one thousand dirhams,' therefore the thousand becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage defines the two functions of the conjunction waw: (1) as a simple sentence connector (عطف الجملة) where it does not create joint participation in the predicate, and (2) as a circumstantial (حال) indicating a condition. Two examples illustrate the first usage: if a man says 'This woman is divorced thrice, and this woman is divorced,' the second divorce is only one because each sentence is independent. In the second example, a woman says 'Divorce me and you have one thousand dirhams' – according to the first interpretation, the waw is a connector and the divorce is without compensation because the default in divorce is that it is gratuitous. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that here waw is circumstantial, meaning 'Divorce me while you have one thousand dirhams,' making the thousand a condition and substitute, thus it becomes obligatory upon the husband. This ikhtilaf is preserved.

Key Terms
واو (waw): A conjunction that can either connect sentences (عطف الجملة) without necessitating shared predicate, or indicate a circumstantial state (حال) making a condition.
عطف الجملة ('atf al-jumlah): Connecting two independent sentences with waw, where each sentence stands alone in its ruling.
حال (hal): A circumstantial clause that provides the condition or state of the main action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example 'Divorce me and you have one thousand dirhams,' according to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the husband entitled to upon divorce?
A) The one thousand dirhams
B) Nothing
C) Half of the thousand
D) It depends on the intention

Key Takeaway
The waw conjunction is ambiguous in legal utterances; its classification as 'atf al-jumlah or hal determines whether the second clause creates a condition, leading to different rulings within the Hanafi school.

The Conjunction Fa in Hanafi Usul
Defines fa for sequential and causal connection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fa and waw in legal utterances and explain how fa's implication of sequential connection and causation is applied in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Fa links cause and effect implying immediate sequence; waw does not.

This passage from Khulasat al-Anwar defines the Arabic conjunction fa (فاء) as a tool for connection and immediate sequence (ta'qib). It illustrates two key applications: one in conditional divorce where the second condition must follow immediately, and another in contract acceptance where fa signals causal acceptance. Understanding the precise Hanafi interpretation of fa is essential for deriving rulings from legal statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary functions of fa
Find in the text the two roles: (1) for connection and immediate sequence (وصل وتعقيب), and (2) used in rulings of causes (احكام العلل).
These are stated directly in the opening and middle of the passage.
2
Analyze the divorce example for sequential condition
Consider the conditional divorce: 'If you enter this house, then this house, then you are divorced.' Note that fa requires immediate entry into the second house after the first without delay.
The condition is 'بلا تراخ' (without delay).
3
Analyze the sale example for causal use
When the seller says 'I sold you this slave for such-and-such' and the buyer replies 'فهو حر' (Then he is free), Hanafi usul interprets this as acceptance of the sale because fa indicates a causal connection.
Contrast with 'وهو حر' (And he is free) which is ambiguous.
4
Understand the distinction between fa and waw
The passage explicitly contrasts fa with waw: waw can be a mere connector without implying sequence or causation, while fa carries the meaning of ta'qib and often causality.
This distinction is critical in evaluating legal utterances.
5
Examine the condition for fa entering upon a cause
Fakhr al-Islam requires the cause to be continuous (دائم), while Sahib al-Tawdih requires it to be final (غائي). The passage gives examples such as 'Pay a thousand, then you are free' where the intended meaning is causal, not temporal.
This nuance affects how fa is applied in deriving rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والفاء للوصل والتعقيب فيتراخى المعطوف عن المعطوف عليه بزمان وان لطف فاذا قال ان دخلت هذه الدار فهذ الدار فأنت طالق فالشرط أن تدخل الثانية بعد الأولى بلا تراخ وتستعمل في احكام العلل فاذاقال بعت منك هذا العبد بكذا وقال الاخر فهو حر يكون قبولاً للبيع . ٢ الفاء : فاء وصل اور تعقیب کیلئے آتی ہے لہذا معطوف معطوف علیہ سے تھوڑا سا زمانہ مؤخر ہوگا لہذا اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا ان دخلت هذه الدار فهذه الدار فأنت طالق تو طلاق کی شرط یہ ہوگی کہ وہ دوسرے گھر میں بغیر تراخی کے پہلے گھر کے بعد داخل ہو۔ اور فا کو اصول احکام میں بھی استعمال کیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ فا تعقیب کیلئے آتی ہے اور احکام علتوں کے بعد آتے ہیں لہذا اگر کسی نے کہا بعت منك هذا العبد بكذا اور شترى نے کہا فھو ر تو یہ بیچ کو قبول کرنا ہو گا لیکن یہاں بیچ کو پہلے اقتضاء مانیں گے کیونکہ حرمت بیچ کے قبول کرنے پر ہی درست ہو سکتی ہے لیکن اگر وهو حر کہا تو پھر قبول کرنا نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں خبر اور انشاء دونوں کا احتمال ہے اس شک کی وجہ سے یہ بیچ کا قبول کرنا نہ ہو گا۔ قوله : وقد تدخل على العلل اذا كانت مما تدوم کبھی فاء ایسی علت پر بھی داخل ہوتی ہے جب کہ علت ایسی ہو جس میں دوام ہوتا ہے که تعقیب کا معنی حاصل ہو سکے مثلاً اگر کسی نے کیا ابشر فقد اتاك الغوث کیونکہ غوث کا آنا اگر چہ وقتی چیز ہے لیکن اس کی ذات دائمی ہے یعنی وہ بشارت سے پہلے بھی ہے اور بعد میں بھی۔ یہ شرط فخر الاسلام کے نزدیک ہے لیکن صاحب توضیح کہتے ہیں کہ فاء کے داخل ہونے کیلئے علت کا غائی ہونا ضروری ہے۔ قوله : كقوله أد الى ألفا فأنت حر أى أدالى ألفا لأنك حر فيعتق في الحال وتستعار بمعنى الواؤ في قوله له على در هم قدر هم حتى لزمه در همان وقا لا لد يتعلقن جميعاً و ينزلن على الترتيب . اسکی مثال ادالى الفافأنت حر يعني ادالى الف لأنك حرتو يه غلام في الحال آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اسکی حرمت ہزار کے ادا کرنے پر موقوف نہیں ہوگی اگر اعتراض ہو کہ کیوں جائز نہیں
His statement: And fa is for connection and immediate sequence, so the conjuncted is delayed relative to the conjuncted to by a time, even if slight. So if he said, 'If you enter this house, then this house, then you are divorced,' the condition is that she enters the second house after the first without delay. And it is used in rulings of causes, so if he said, 'I sold you this slave for such-and-such' and the other said, 'Then he is free,' it becomes acceptance of the sale. 2. Fa: Fa is for connection and immediate sequence, therefore the conjuncted will be slightly delayed from the conjuncted to. So if someone said to his wife, 'If you enter this house, then this house, then you are divorced,' the condition for divorce is that she enters the second house without delay after the first. And fa is also used in principles of rulings, because fa is for immediate sequence and rulings come after causes. So if someone said, 'I sold you this slave for such-and-such' and the buyer said, 'Then he is free,' this will be acceptance of the sale. But here we will consider the sale first as required, because the validity of the sale depends on acceptance. But if he said, 'And he is free,' then acceptance will not occur, because in that there is probability of both report and directive; due to this doubt, it will not be acceptance of the sale. His statement: And it may enter upon causes when they are continuous. Sometimes fa enters upon a cause that is continuous, so that the meaning of immediate sequence can be achieved. For example, if someone said, 'Rejoice, for help has come to you,' because the arrival of help, although a momentary thing, its essence is continuous, meaning it exists before the glad tidings and after. This is the condition according to Fakhr al-Islam, but Sahib al-Tawdih says that for fa to enter, the cause must be final (gha'i). His statement: Such as his saying, 'Pay a thousand dirhams, then you are free,' meaning pay a thousand dirhams because you are free, so he is freed immediately. And it is used metaphorically in the meaning of waw in his saying: 'He has a dirham and a dirham' until two dirhams become due, and they said: they all become connected and are arranged in order. Its example: 'Pay a thousand dirhams, then you are free' means pay a thousand because you are free, so this slave is freed immediately, and his freedom is not dependent on paying the thousand. If an objection is raised: why is it not permissible...
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage defines the conjunction fa and its two main functions: (1) indicating sequential order with a slight time gap, and (2) entering upon a cause to connect it to its effect. The first function is illustrated with a conditional divorce: 'If you enter this house, then this house, then you are divorced' – the divorce only occurs if the second house is entered immediately after the first. The second function applies in legal transactions: if a seller says 'I sold you this slave for such-and-such' and the buyer replies 'Then he is free,' it is considered acceptance of the sale because fa signals a cause-effect relationship. However, if the buyer says 'And he is free' using waw, it is ambiguous and does not constitute acceptance. The passage also discusses a subtle condition from Fakhr al-Islam that the cause must be continuous for fa to enter, but Sahib al-Tawdih requires the cause to be final (ghai). An example is given: 'Pay a thousand dirhams, then you are free' – though fa suggests sequence, the intended meaning is 'Pay a thousand because you are free,' so freedom occurs immediately upon the statement, not upon payment. This shows the metaphorical use of fa in the meaning of waw for causation.

Key Terms
الفاء (al-fa): A conjunction that indicates connection and immediate sequence (تعقيب), used to link causes to effects or actions in order.
تعقيب (ta'qib): Immediate succession without significant delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is a rejection
C) It is ambiguous
D) It is a counteroffer

Key Takeaway
The conjunction fa in Hanafi usul is a key indicator of immediate sequence and causation, distinguishing it from mere conjunction waw.

Fa for Immediate Succession in Conditions and Contracts
Explains fa as conjunction and immediate succession with divorce and sale examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that 'fa' requires immediate succession (ta'qib) to distinguish valid from invalid conditional statements and contracts.

Core Idea
Fa demands immediate succession — a delay breaks the condition or invalidates the acceptance.

In Hanafi usul, the particle 'fa' (فاء) is not a neutral conjunction: it carries a specific legal meaning of immediate succession. This lesson examines two key applications: conditional divorce and sale acceptance. Understanding when 'fa' is used versus 'waw' can determine the validity of a legal act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule about fa
The passage states that 'fa' indicates immediate succession (ta'qib) — the second event must follow the first without delay.
This distinguishes it from 'waw' (simple conjunction) and 'thumma' (delayed succession).
2
Apply the rule to divorce condition
In the example 'If you enter this house, then this house, then you are divorced,' fa requires immediate entry into the second house after the first. A delay breaks the condition.
The condition is not fulfilled if there is any time gap.
3
Apply the rule to sale acceptance
When the seller says 'I sold you this slave for such-and-such' and the buyer responds with 'fa-huwa hurr (then he is free),' fa indicates acceptance of the sale because the ruling (freedom) follows the cause (sale) immediately.
If 'waw' is used instead ('wa huwa hurr'), it is ambiguous and not considered acceptance.
4
Understand the usul principle
The passage notes that 'fa' is used in usul to connect rulings (ahkam) to their causes (ilal) — another application of immediate succession.
Rulings are understood to follow their causes without delay in legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢ الفاء : فاء وصل اور تعقیب کیلئے آتی ہے لہذا معطوف معطوف علیہ سے تھوڑا سا زمانہ مؤخر ہوگا لہذا اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا ان دخلت هذه الدار فهذه الدار فأنت طالق تو طلاق کی شرط یہ ہوگی کہ وہ دوسرے گھر میں بغیر تراخی کے پہلے گھر کے بعد داخل ہو۔ اور فضا کو اصول احکام میں بھی استعمال کیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ فا تعقیب کیلئے آتی ہے اور احکام علتوں کے بعد آتے ہیں لہذا اگر کسی نے کہا بعت منك هذا العبد بكذا اور شترى نے کہا فھو ر تو یہ بیچ کو قبول کرنا ہو گا لیکن یہاں بیچ کو پہلے اقتضاء مانیں گے کیونکہ حرمت بیچ کے قبول کرنے پر ہی درست ہو سکتی ہے لیکن اگر وهو حر کہا تو پھر قبول کرنا نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس میں خبر اور انشاء دونوں کا احتمال ہے اس شک کی وجہ سے یہ بیچ کا قبول کرنا نہ ہو گا۔
2. Al-Fa: Fa comes for conjunction and immediate succession, so the conjunct is slightly delayed from the conjoined. So if someone said to his wife: 'If you enter this house, then this house, then you are divorced,' the condition for divorce will be that she enters the second house immediately after the first house without delay. And fa is also used in the principles of rulings because fa comes for immediate succession, and rulings come after causes. So if someone said: 'I sold you this slave for such-and-such' and the buyer said: 'then he is free,' this would be acceptance of the sale. But here we consider the sale to require prior demand, because the legality of the sale is only valid upon acceptance. However, if he said: 'and he is free,' then it would not be acceptance, because it has the probability of both [declarative and performative] due to doubt, so this would not be acceptance of the sale.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage explains the primary use of the Arabic particle 'fa' (فاء) for immediate succession. In the Hanafi madhhab, when used in conditional sentences, 'fa' requires that the consequence follow the condition without any significant time gap. The example of divorce shows that if a man says to his wife, 'If you enter this house, then this house, then you are divorced,' the divorce only occurs if she enters the second house directly after the first, without delay. The same principle applies in contracts: if a seller says 'I sold you this slave for such-and-such' and the buyer responds 'then he is free,' it is considered acceptance of the sale because the 'fa' indicates immediate succession of the ruling (freedom) after the cause (sale). However, if the buyer says 'and he is free' using 'waw', it is not valid as acceptance because 'waw' does not imply succession and could be a separate statement. The passage also notes that 'fa' is used in usul to connect rulings (ahkam) to their causes (ilal). This is a Zahir al-Riwayah ruling based on standard linguistic principles.

Key Terms
الفاء (al-fa): A conjunction particle that implies immediate succession (تعقیب) between two clauses without delay.
تعقیب (ta'qib): The quality of immediate succession; the second event occurs right after the first without any intervening time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because 'waw' does not indicate immediate succession and the statement could be a separate declaration.
C) Because the buyer did not say 'I accept' explicitly.
D) Because the sale was invalid due to defective offer.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'fa' in Hanafi usul imposes immediate succession (ta'qib), affecting the validity of conditions and contracts.

Fa Entering on Enduring Causes – The Condition of Continuity and Finality
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition for fa entering on causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi conditions for fa entering on causes (dawam vs gha'i) and explain their legal implications.

Core Idea
Fa indicates immediate succession, but can enter on a cause only if the cause is enduring or final.

The particle fa primarily signals immediate succession (ta'qib). However, when it enters on a cause (illa), Hanafi usul scholars debate what type of cause permits this. Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi requires the cause to have continuity (dawam), while Sadr al-Shariah in al-Tawdih demands it be a final cause (gha'i). Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to analyze legal conditionals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that we are analyzing the particle fa when it precedes a cause (illa). The core question: under what conditions can fa enter upon a cause while retaining its meaning of immediate succession?
This is a purely usul al-fiqh inquiry, not a specific ruling.
2
State Fakhr al-Islam's condition
Fakhr al-Islam requires the cause to be enduring (dawam), meaning it exists before and after the consequence, so that 'immediate succession' is meaningful.
Example: 'Rejoice, for relief has come' – relief endures, so fa works.
3
State Sadr al-Shariah's condition
Sadr al-Shariah (author of al-Tawdih) disagrees, requiring the cause to be final (gha'i), i.e., the purpose or goal.
This is a more restrictive condition than mere continuity.
4
Compare the two conditions
Consider a cause that endures but is not final – would it satisfy Sadr al-Shariah? No. Thus the two conditions yield different scopes.
The practical difference emerges in cases where a cause is enduring but not contractual or purposive.
5
Determine the preferred view
The text does not explicitly choose, but presents both as valid Hanafi positions. Later usul works often adopt Sadr al-Shariah's view as more precise.
In fatwa, the mufti may follow either depending on context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وقد تدخل على العلل اذا كانت مما تدوم كبھی فاء ایسی علت پر بھی داخل ہوتی ہے جب کہ علت ایسی ہو جس میں درام ہوتا ہے كه تعقیب کا معنی حاصل ہو سكے مثلاً اگر کسی نے کیا ابشر فقد اتاك الغوث کیونکہ غوث کا آنا اگر چہ وقتی چیز ہے لیکن اس کی ذات دائگی ہے یعنی وہ بشارت سے پہلے بھی ہے اور بعد میں بھی۔ یہ شرط فخر الاسلام کے نزدیک ہے لیکن صاحب توضیح کہتے ہیں کہ فاء کے داخل ہونے کیلئے علت کا غائی ہونا ضروری ہے۔ قوله : كقوله أد الى ألفا فأنت حر أى أدالى ألفا لأنك حر فيعتق في الحال وتستعار بمعنى الواؤ في قوله له على در هم قدر هم حتی لزمه در همان وقا لا لد يتعلقن جميعاً و ينزلن على الترتيب . اسکی مثال ادالى الفافأنت حر يعني ادالى الف لأنك حرتو يه غلام في الحال آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اسکی حرمت ہزار کے ادا کرنے پر موقوف نہیں ہوگی اگر اعتراض ہو کہ کیوں جائز نہیں کہ اسکی تقدیر یوں ہو ان ادیت الفا فأنت (حر) تو جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ جواب امر کا مستحق ہو ہی اس وقت سکتا ہے جب کہ کلمہ ان کو مقدر مانا جائے اور کلمہ ان لفظ ہو تو وہ ماضی کو اور جملہ اسمیہ کو مستقبل کے معنی میں کر دیتا ہے اور اگر مقدر ہو تو مستقبل کے معنی میں نہیں کر سکتا تو جب وہ مستقبل کے معنی میں نہیں ہوگا تو جواب امر میں بھی واقع نہیں ہوگا۔ اور فاء کو مجاز و او کے معنی میں بھی تعمال کیا جاتا ہے جیسے کہ اگر کسی نے کہا (علی در هم قدر هم ) تو یہاں فار تعقیب کیلئے نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ تعقیب اعراض میں ہوتی ہے اعیان میں نہیں ہوتی جب کہ درحم مین ہے لہذا فاء داؤ کے معنی میں ہوگی اور اس پر دو درهم واجب ہو نگے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہاں جب فاء کے حقیقی معنی ممکن نہیں ہے تو اسکو تاکید کیلئے استعمال کرینگے لہذا صرف ایک درھم واجب ہوگا۔
He said: And fa may enter upon causes if they are enduring. Sometimes fa enters on a cause that is such that there is continuity, so that the meaning of immediate succession can be obtained. For example, if someone said: 'Rejoice, for relief has come to you,' because the coming of relief, although it is a temporal thing, its essence is perpetual, meaning it exists before the good news and after it. This is the condition according to Fakhr al-Islam, but the author of al-Tawdih says that for fa to enter, the cause must be final (gha'i). He said: Like his saying: 'Pay one thousand, then you are free,' meaning 'Pay one thousand because you are free,' so the slave becomes free immediately, and it is used metaphorically in the sense of waw. In his saying: 'He owes a dirham, then a dirham' until two dirhams become obligatory, and they say they are both binding and imposed in order. Its example: 'Pay one thousand then you are free' means 'Pay one thousand because you are free,' so this slave becomes free immediately, and his freedom is not conditional upon paying the thousand. If it is objected: 'Why is it not permissible that its implied meaning be 'If you pay one thousand, then you are free'?' The answer is: The response to a command can only occur when the word 'in' is implied, and the word 'in' when explicit makes the past tense and nominal sentence into future meaning, but if implied, it cannot give future meaning. So when it is not in future meaning, it cannot occur as a response to a command. And fa is also used metaphorically in the sense of waw, as when someone says: 'He owes a dirham, then a dirham.' Here fa cannot be for immediate succession because immediate succession applies to accidents, not entities, and the dirham is an entity. Therefore fa will be in the meaning of waw, and two dirhams become obligatory. Imam Shafi'i says: Since the literal meaning of fa is not possible here, we will use it for emphasis, so only one dirham is obligatory.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage discusses two advanced usages of fa. First, it can enter upon causes (ilal) that are enduring, meaning the cause exists before and after the consequence. Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi conditions that the cause must have continuity (dawam) to allow the meaning of immediate succession (ta'qib). Sadr al-Shariah in al-Tawdih disagrees, requiring the cause to be final (gha'i) rather than enduring. This is a dispute within the Hanafi school. Second, fa can be used metaphorically in the sense of waw (simple conjunction) when literal succession is impossible. The example: 'Pay one thousand, then you are free' (اد إلى ألفا فأنت حر). In this statement, the fa cannot indicate succession because freedom is not a result of payment; rather, it is the cause. The Hanafis interpret it as metaphorical fa, making the slave free immediately. An objection suggests it could be conditional ('If you pay, then you are free'), but the text refutes this because the implied 'in' (if) cannot give future meaning when not explicit. Another example: 'He owes a dirham, then a dirham' (على درهم فدرهم). Since a dirham is an entity (ayn) and succession applies to accidents (a'rad), fa here means waw, so two dirhams are owed. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, considering fa as emphatic, thus only one dirham. This is a well-known ikhtilaf in Hanafi usul. The authority weight is from the later Hanafi tradition (mutakhkhirin), reflecting commentary on earlier works.

Key Terms
علة غائية (illa gha'iyya): A cause that is final or teleological, as distinct from an efficient cause.
استعارة (isti'ara): Metaphorical usage, where a word is used in a non-literal sense due to a relationship of similarity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sadr al-Shariah, what type of cause must fa enter upon?
A) An enduring cause (dawam)
B) A final cause (gha'i)
C) Any cause that exists
D) A cause that is an accident

Key Takeaway
Fa can enter a cause only if the cause is either enduring (Fakhr al-Islam) or final (Sadr al-Shariah), two valid Hanafi positions.

Metaphorical Use of Fa as Waw – Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the metaphorical use of fa as waw.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi interpretation of fa as waw when literal succession is impossible, and contrast it with the Shafi'i view of emphasis.

Core Idea
When literal fa is impossible, Hanafis take it as waw (and) while Shafi'is take it as emphasis, leading to different legal consequences.

This lesson dives into a classic usul dispute concerning the particle fa in phrases like 'على درهم فدرهم' (he owes a dirham, then a dirham). Since dirhams are physical objects, immediate succession between them is impossible; Hanafis therefore interpret fa metaphorically as waw, making two dirhams obligatory. Imam Shafi'i argues that when literal meaning fails, fa is used for emphasis, yielding only one dirham. The practical difference (thamarah) is clear in loan and guarantee contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed phrase
Focus on the phrase 'على درهم فدرهم' (he owes a dirham, then a dirham). The particle fa connects two nouns (dirhams).
This is a constructed legal example, not a Quranic verse.
2
Explain why literal fa is impossible
The literal meaning of fa is immediate succession (ta'qib). Succession applies to events (a'rad), not to physical objects (a'yan). Since dirham is a fixed entity, it cannot follow itself in time.
Hanafi usul uses the rule: 'al-ta'qib fi al-a'rad la fi al-a'yan'.
3
State the Hanafi interpretation
Since literal meaning is impossible, fa is used metaphorically (isti'ara) in the sense of waw (simple conjunction). Thus two dirhams are owed.
The metaphorical shift preserves the additive sense but removes temporal ordering.
4
State the Shafi'i interpretation
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that when the literal meaning cannot apply, fa is used for emphasis (tawkid), reinforcing the single amount. So only one dirham is owed.
For Shafi'is, emphasis is a common secondary function of fa.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
In a loan contract, Hanafis rule that two dirhams are due; Shafi'is rule one. This directly affects financial obligations.
The dispute is purely interpretative; both schools have consistent usul principles.

The Particle 'Faa': When Immediate Succession Becomes Conjunction
Explains the legal usul meaning of 'faa' and a dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for the particle 'faa' when immediate succession is impossible, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
When 'faa' cannot indicate immediate succession, Hanafi usul shifts it to the meaning of 'waw' (and), doubling the obligation.

The Arabic particle 'faa' (فاء) typically denotes immediate succession (ta'qib). However, in legal interpretation, its meaning can shift when the context makes immediate succession impossible. This lesson explores the Hanafi rule that 'faa' is then used metaphorically as 'waw' (and), and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view that it becomes emphatic. Understanding this distinction is crucial for deriving correct rulings from linguistically ambiguous texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic context
Find the statement where 'faa' is used and determine whether the objects involved are accidents (a'rad) or substances (a'yan). This is the critical factor.
Accidents include actions, events; substances include physical objects like dirhams.
2
Test the possibility of immediate succession
If the context involves substances, immediate succession is impossible because ta'qib only applies to accidents. If accidents, the literal meaning holds.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
When the literal meaning is impossible, 'faa' is considered majaz (metaphorical) and takes the meaning of 'waw' (and) by 'urf and qiyas.
This results in conjunction, not sequential order.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that when the real meaning is impossible, 'faa' is used for emphasis (tawkid), not as 'waw'.
This leads to a different number of obligations.
5
Derive the practical ruling
In the example, Hanafi: two dirhams due; Shafi'i: one dirham due. The thamarah al-khilaf is one dirham.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کہ اسکی تقدیر یوں ہو ان ادیت الفا فأنت (حر) تو جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ جواب امر کا مستحق ہو ہی اس وقت سکتا ہے جب کہ کلمہ ان کو مقدر مانا جائے اور کلمہ ان لفظ ہو تو وہ ماضی کو اور جملہ اسمیہ کو مستقبل کے معنی میں کر دیتا ہے اور اگر مقدر ہو تو مستقبل کے معنی میں نہیں کر سکتا تو جب وہ مستقبل کے معنی میں نہیں ہوگا تو جواب امر میں بھی واقع نہیں ہوگا۔ اور فاء کو مجاز و او کے معنی میں بھی تعمال کیا جاتا ہے جیسے کہ اگر کسی نے کہا (علی در هم قدر هم ) تو یہاں فار تعقیب کیلئے نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ تعقیب اعراض میں ہوتی ہے اعیان میں نہیں ہوتی جب کہ درحم مین ہے لہذا فاء داؤ کے معنی میں ہوگی اور اس پر دو درهم واجب ہو نگے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہاں جب فاء کے حقیقی معنی ممکن نہیں ہے تو اسکو تاکید کیلئے استعمال کرینگے لہذا صرف ایک درھم واجب ہوگا۔
That its appreciation is such that if you pay the thousand, then you are free. The answer to this is that the answer to a command can only be deserving when the word 'in' is considered estimative. And the word 'in' makes the past and the nominal sentence into future meaning. And if it is estimative, it cannot make it future. So when it is not in future meaning, it will not occur as the answer to the command. And 'faa' is used metaphorically in the meaning of 'waw'. For example, if someone said 'upon me a dirham, its value' then here 'faa' cannot be for immediate succession because immediate succession occurs in accidents, not in substances, since dirham is a substance. Therefore, 'faa' will be in the meaning of 'waw', and two dirhams become obligatory upon him. And Imam Shafi'i says that here when the real meaning of 'faa' is not possible, we use it for emphasis, so only one dirham is obligatory.

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul rule regarding the particle 'faa' (فاء). The author first explains a conditional sentence involving 'in' (if) and the response, noting that 'in' affects verb tense. Then the central point: 'faa' can be used metaphorically like 'waw' meaning 'and' when its primary meaning of immediate succession is impossible. The example: if someone says 'upon me a dirham, its value' (likely a conditional or oath?), here 'faa' cannot indicate immediate succession because dirham is a substance (عين), and immediate succession pertains to accidents (أعراض). Therefore, 'faa' takes the meaning of 'waw', resulting in two dirhams due. Imam Shafi'i counters that when the real meaning is impossible, 'faa' is used for emphasis (تاكيد), so only one dirham is due. The Hanafi position is that consequential meaning is preferred over emphasis in such cases.

Key Terms
فاء (faa): Particle of immediate succession (تعقیب), but can be used metaphorically as 'waw' (واو) for conjunction or causality when immediate succession is impossible.

The Particle 'Bal': Definition and Legal Consequences in Divorce
Defines the legal impact of 'bal' in statements, applying it to divorce examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of 'bal' in legal statements and apply it to distinguish between divorce and debt contexts, determining the correct number of divorces.

Core Idea
'Bal' affirms the next statement but does not nullify the prior in divorce — accumulation results.

The simple word 'bal' (rather/but rather) carries a precise legal meaning in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. In everyday speech it corrects a mistake, but in law its effect depends on the context. This lesson unpacks the definition of 'bal' and shows how it leads to three divorces in a common scenario, while in debts the first statement is completely replaced.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of 'bal'
Read the passage carefully: 'bal' affirms what comes after it and turns away from what precedes it in a corrective manner. The speaker implies that the first part was a mistake and the second is the intended truth.
This definition is from Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
2
Apply to the divorce example
Consider the statement: 'You are divorced once, rather twice.' According to Hanafi law, the first divorce (one) is already effective and cannot be undone. Therefore, 'rather twice' adds an additional two divorces, totaling three. The first is not cancelled because divorce rights are already exercised.
The wife must be consummated for this ruling to apply.
3
Contrast with the debt example
If someone says 'I owe one thousand, rather two thousand,' only the second amount (two thousand) is considered his debt. The first amount is abrogated because it was a mistake and no obligation had been fulfilled yet.
This illustrates that the effect of 'bal' depends on whether the first act can be undone.
4
Examine the negative sentence case
In a negative sentence like 'Zaid did not come to me, rather Amr,' there is disagreement: some say both are negated (Amr also did not come), others say Amr is affirmed (only Amr came). The Hanafi tarjih is not settled in this text, but it highlights the linguistic ambiguity.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf among scholars.

His saying: And 'bal' is for affirming what comes after it and turning away from what comes before it in the manner of correction. So three divorces occur when a man says to his consummated wife: 'You are divorced once, rather twice' because he did not have the power to nullify the first, so both fall. Unlike his saying 'I have upon me one thousand, rather two thousand.' 'Bal': 'Bal' comes to affirm what is after it and to turn away from what is before it in the manner of correction, that is, to express that in what came before 'bal' there was a mistake because it was not intended, but rather what was meant was what follows. For example: 'Zaid came to me, rather Amr' – for travel? Then negativeness is established, and Zaid has two possibilities. But if the sentence is negative, i.e., 'Zaid did not come to me, rather Amr', then some people say the negation is directed towards Amr, and some say affirmation is directed towards Amr. Application: If a man said to his consummated wife, 'You are divorced once, rather twice', three divorces occur.

Commentary
This passage defines the legal effect of the word 'bal' (rather, but rather) in speech. According to the Hanafi school, 'bal' serves to affirm what follows it and to correct what preceded it, as if the speaker made a mistake. In divorce, if a man says to his wife 'You are divorced once, rather twice', both divorces occur, because the first is not nullified and the second is added, totaling three (since 'rather twice' establishes an additional two?) Wait, the text says 'three divorces occur'. Explanation: In Hanafi, if a man says 'you are divorced once, rather twice' to a consummated wife, the first one counts as one, and the second phrase 'rather twice' establishes two divorces, but since the first is not revoked, the total becomes three. The passage contrasts this with a debt example: if someone says 'I owe one thousand, rather two thousand', he does not become liable for three thousand; only the last amount is established because in debts, the first is effectively cancelled. In divorce, however, the first divorce cannot be withdrawn, so both are effective. The text also discusses negative sentences: if one says 'Zaid did not come to me, rather Amr', there is disagreement whether Amr is also negated or affirmed. The lesson concludes with the application: three divorces occur.

Key Terms
بل (bal): A particle of interjection meaning 'rather' or 'but rather', used to correct the preceding statement and affirm the following.

The Particle 'Laken' and Its Legal Applications
Defining the Arabic particle 'laken' with conditions for conjunctive use and legal application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions for 'laken' to function as a conjunction and apply the correct interpretation of a master's statement in a marriage contract scenario.

Core Idea
'Laken' only connects when the negation and affirmation are about different things; otherwise, it starts a new statement.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text dissects the Arabic particle 'laken', distinguishing its conjunctive and inceptive uses. Understanding this distinction is critical for interpreting legal statements correctly. The example of a master's response to his slave-girl's unauthorized marriage illustrates how a seemingly contradictory phrase can be legally resolved.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two forms of 'laken'
Identify that 'laken' can be light (mukhaffaf, conjunctive) or heavy (mushaddad, inceptive). The light form connects clauses; the heavy form starts a new independent statement.
The heavy form is among the particles resembling verbs (inna wa akhawatuha).
2
State the conditions for conjunctive 'laken'
List the two conditions: (1) the entire speech must be coherent and connected; (2) the negation must apply to one thing and the affirmation to another different thing.
If either condition fails, 'laken' is inceptive.
3
Apply conditions to the slave-girl example
Analyze the master's statement: 'I do not authorize the marriage, but I authorize it for 150 dirhams.' Here, both negation and affirmation refer to the same act (authorizing the marriage), so condition (2) fails. Therefore 'laken' is inceptive.
The contradiction in referring to the same act forces an interpretation of annulment followed by a new contract.
4
Determine the legal outcome
Because 'laken' is inceptive, the first part 'I do not authorize the marriage' stands alone as an annulment of the original marriage. The second part 'I authorize it for 150 dirhams' is a new independent statement forming a new marriage contract with a dower of 150 dirhams.
Thus the original marriage is dissolved and a new one is created.
5
Distinguish from the alternative statement
Contrast with: 'I do not authorize it for 100, but I authorize it for 150.' Here the negation is about the dower amount (100) and the affirmation about a different amount (150), satisfying condition (2). Hence 'laken' is conjunctive, and the original marriage remains valid with the modified dower of 150 dirhams.
The negation is restricted to the dower, not the marriage itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لیکن :
لكن نفی کے بعد استدراک کیلئے آتا ہے یعنی سابق سے جو و ہم پیدا ہوا ہو اس کو دور کر نے کیلئے آتا ہے جیسے قول ما جاء فى زيد لكن عمر وا پھر اگر یہ مخففہ ہو تو عاطفہ ہوگا اور اگر مشدودہ ہو تو حروف مشبہ با فعل میں سے ہوگا۔ لیکن یہ عطف اس وقت صحیح ہو گا جب کہ کلام مرتب ہو یعنی سابق کلام کیساتھ متصل ہو اور نفی ایک چیز کی ہو اور اثبات اس کے علاوہ دوسری چیز کا ہو۔
اگر ان دونوں شرطوں میں سے ایک شرط بھی نہ پائی گئی تو کلام مستانفہ ہو گا معطوفہ نہیں ہوگا
مثلاً اگر کسی لونڈی نے اپنے مولی کی اجازت کے بغیہ سود در هم پر نکاح کر لیا اور موٹی نے كيا لا اجيز النكاح ولكن اجيزه بمائة وخمسین درهما ) تو یہ نکاح کو فسخ کرنا ہوگا (لكن)) متانفہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ بعینہ ایک ہی فعل کی نفی اور اس کا اثبات ہے تو اول کلام آخر کلام سے متناقض ہو جائیگا لہذا ہم یوں سمجھیں گے کہ مولی نے پہلے نکاح کو فسخ کر دیا اور پھرنے مہر پر دوسرا نکاح کیا لیکن اگر مولی نے اسکے جواب میں کہا ( لا اجيز النكاح بمائة ولكن اجيزه بمائة و خمسين در هما) تو اصل نکاح باقی رہے گا اور نفی صرف مائتہ کی قید کی ہو گی ۔
Because in news, one can turn away from the previous, but in this turning away... but if someone said 'one thousand' or 'two thousand', then only two thousand becomes binding because it is confession and news, so turning away from the previous is possible. His statement: 'But (laken) is for istidrak (correction) after negation, except that conjunction is when the speech is coherent, otherwise it is independent. For example, a slave-girl who married without her master's permission for one hundred dirhams, and he said: 'I do not authorize the marriage, but I authorize it for one hundred and fifty dirhams.' This is an annulment of the marriage, and they made 'laken' as the beginning of a new sentence because this is in the negation and affirmation of the very same action. Laken: Laken comes after negation for correction, i.e., to remove any misconception that arose from the previous. For example, the statement: 'Zaid did not come, but 'Amr did.' Then if it is light (mukhaffafa), it is a conjunction particle, and if it is heavy (mushaddada), it is among the particles resembling verbs. But this conjunction is only valid when the speech is connected, i.e., it is connected with the previous clause, and the negation is for one thing and the affirmation is for another thing besides it. If one of these two conditions is not found, then the speech is independent, not conjunctive. For example, if a slave-girl married without her master's permission for one hundred dirhams, and the master said: 'I do not authorize the marriage, but I authorize it for one hundred and fifty dirhams,' then this is an annulment of the marriage. 'Laken' is independent because it is the negation and affirmation of the very same action; so the first statement and the last statement become contradictory. Therefore, we understand that the master first annulled the marriage and then contracted a new marriage with a different dower. But if the master said in response: 'I do not authorize the marriage for one hundred, but I authorize it for one hundred and fifty dirhams,' then the original marriage remains, and the negation is only restricted to the hundred.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul work analyzes the Arabic particle 'laken'. It is classified as a textual analysis because it explains the linguistic and legal implications of a grammatical particle. The author clarifies that 'laken' after negation serves to correct a misunderstanding from the preceding statement. It can be either light (conjunctive) or heavy (non-conjunctive). For it to function as a conjunction, two conditions must be met: the speech must be coherent and connected, and the negation must apply to one thing while the affirmation applies to another. If these conditions are not met, 'laken' starts a new independent statement. The key example is a slave-girl marrying without permission for 100 dirhams. If the master says 'I do not authorize the marriage, but I authorize it for 150 dirhams', this is contradictory because it negates and affirms the same act. Hence, it is interpreted as an annulment followed by a new contract. If he says 'I do not authorize it for 100, but I authorize it for 150', the negation is limited to the dower amount, so the original marriage stands with a different dower. This demonstrates how linguistic particles shape legal outcomes in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
لكن (laken): Particle for istidrak (correction) after negation; can be conjunctive (light form) or inceptive (heavy form).

The Hanafi Analysis of 'Aw' (or) in Legal Texts
Defining 'aw' and its legal applications in agency and sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi classification of the particle 'aw', distinguish it from doubt, and apply its ruling in agency, sale, and lease contracts.

Core Idea
'Aw' means one of the mentioned items, not doubt; it validates agency but invalidates sale unless choice is limited.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi treatment of the particle 'aw' (or). You will learn why Hanafi usul rejects the notion that 'aw' primarily indicates doubt, and how this affects legal statements, especially in contracts like agency and sale.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
The author states 'aw' is for one of the mentioned items. Example: pointing to two slaves and saying 'this is free or this' means one becomes free.
The ruling is for one of the two, not both.
2
Reject the doubt view
Some scholars claim 'aw' indicates doubt, but Hanafi usul argues that doubt is not the speaker's intent; if doubt were intended, the word 'shakk' exists separately.
Doubt may be implied by context but is not the primary meaning.
3
Distinguish constructive vs. informative
The initial statement is constructive (insha) but requires later clarification, which is treated as informative (khabar) and binding. The speaker must specify which item is intended, and the subject must be capable of accepting the ruling.
If one slave dies before clarification, the later claim to have intended the dead one is rejected.
4
Apply to agency
When 'aw' is used in agency (e.g., 'I appoint this or that person as agent'), it is valid. Each agent can act independently because agency is constructive and 'aw' grants choice.
Agency is an insha', so 'aw' gives option to either agent.
5
Apply to sale and lease
Using 'aw' in sale (e.g., 'I sold this or this') or lease (e.g., 'for a thousand or two thousand') creates uncertainty in object or price, rendering the contract void. Exception: if a right of choice (khiyar) is specified for up to three options, it is valid by istihsan.
More than three options (e.g., superior, medium, inferior) is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وأو لأحد المذكورين وقوله هذا حر او هذا كقولها هما حر و جعل البيان انشاء من وجه واخبار من وجه واذا دخلت فى الوكالة يصح بخلاف البيع والاجارة الا أن يكون من له الخيار معلوماً فى اثنين أو ثلاثة فيصح استحساناً
أو :
اور ( أو ) احد المذکورین کیلئے آتا ہے یعنی جن دو چیزوں کو (أو) کے ذریعے ذکر کیا گیا ہے حکم کو ان میں سے ایک کیلئے ثابت کرتا ہے۔ جیسے اگر کسی نے اپنے دو غلاموں کی طرف اشارہ کر کے کہا هذا حر أو هذا تو ان میں سے ایک آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
بعض علماء کہتے ہیں کہ ( أو ) کو شک کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے لیکن یہ بات صحیح نہیں اسلئے کہ شک متکلم کا مقصود نہیں ہوتا بلکہ حمل کلام سے لازم آتا ہے اور اگر شک مقصود بھی ہو تو اس کے لئے ( شک ) کا لفظ موجود ہے اور یہ کلام چونکہ انشاء کا بھی احتمال رکھتا ہے اور خبر کا بھی لہذا متکلم کی طرف سے تعین ضروری ہے ۔ کہ وہ بیان کرے کہ ان میں سے کون سا غلام مراد ہے۔ اور اس مقام پر متکلم کے بیان کو من وجہ انشاء اور من وجہ اخبار سمجھا جاتا ہے گویا کہ عنق اب پایا جارہا ہے۔ لہذا یہ شرط ہے کہ حمل محق کو قبول کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو تو اگر دونوں میں سے ایک غلام مر گیا اور پھر متکلم نے کہا کہ یہی غلام میری مراد تھا تو اس کی بات کو قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور چونکہ یہ من وجہ اخبار ہے لہذا قاضی اس کو غلام کے آزاد کرنے پر مجبور کر سکتا ہے۔ جب حرف ( أو ) وکالت پر داخل ہو تو بھی صحیح ہوگا اور ان دونوں وکیلوں میں سے ہر ایک کو تصرف کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا کیونکہ توکیل بھی انشاء ہے اور انشاء میں وتخییر کیلئے ہوتا ہے، بخلاف ریچ اور اجارہ نے کہ اس میں یہ نہیں کہہ سکتا بعت هذا أو هذا او اجرت هذا بالف او بالفین کیونکہ معقود علیہ اور معقود بہ مجہول رہ جائے گا لیکن اگر من له الخيار معلوم ہو تو دو یا تین مبیع اور ثمن میں او کالا ناصحیح ہوگا لیکن اسے زیادہ میں صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ تین جید متوسط اور ردی پر
His statement: 'And 'aw' is for one of the mentioned [items].' And his statement: 'This is free or this,' like his statement: 'Both are free.' And they made the explanation constructive from one perspective and informative from another. And when it enters into agency, it is valid, unlike sale and lease, unless the one with the right of choice is known among two or three, then it is valid by istihsan. 'Aw': 'Aw' comes for one of the mentioned items, i.e., it establishes the ruling for one of the two things mentioned with 'aw'. For example, if someone points to his two slaves and says: 'This is free or this,' one of them becomes free. Some scholars say that 'aw' is placed for doubt, but this is not correct because doubt is not intended by the speaker; rather it is implied by the context of the speech. And if doubt is intended, there is the word 'doubt' available. And since this speech can potentially be constructive or informative, specification by the speaker is necessary: he must clarify which slave is intended. In this context, the speaker's explanation is considered constructive in one aspect and informative in another, as if it is happening imminently. Therefore, it is a condition that the subject is capable of accepting the ruling. So if one of the two slaves dies and then the speaker says that this was the one he intended, his statement is not accepted. And because it is informative in one aspect, the judge can compel him to free the slave. When the particle 'aw' enters into agency, it is also valid, and each of the two agents has the authority to act, because agency is also constructive and in constructive contexts 'aw' is for choice. Unlike sale and lease, where one cannot say 'I sold this or this' or 'I leased this for a thousand or two thousand' because the object and the price would remain unknown. However, if the one with the right of choice is known among two or three, then it is valid by istihsan, but it is not valid for more than that because of three grades: superior, medium, and inferior.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage analyzes the Arabic particle 'aw' (or) in legal contexts. The author states that 'aw' indicates one of the mentioned items, not doubt as some scholars claim. In Hanafi usul, the speaker must clarify which item is intended when using 'aw' in declarative statements. The passage distinguishes between constructive (insha) and informative (khabar) aspects: the initial statement is constructive, but when the speaker later clarifies, that clarification is treated as informative, making it binding. A key example is freeing one of two slaves: if one slave dies, the speaker's later claim to have intended the dead one is not accepted because the subject must be capable at the time of the statement. 'Aw' is valid in agency (each agent can act independently) because agency is constructive and 'aw' grants choice. However, in sale and lease, using 'aw' creates uncertainty in the object or price, rendering the contract void unless a right of choice (khiyar) is specified for a limited number of options (two or three) by istihsan. This shows how linguistic particles affect contract validity in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
أو (aw): Particle for one of the mentioned items, indicating choice or uncertainty depending on context.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the particle 'aw' signifies one of the mentioned items, not doubt; in constructive contexts it grants choice, but in informative contexts it requires clarification.

The Particle 'Aw' in Hanafi Usul: Takhyir vs Doubt
Expansion of rule on 'aw' in legal declarations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that 'aw' in insha' (performative speech) indicates takhyir, and apply this rule to distinguish valid uses (e.g., wakalah, limited khyar) from invalid ones (e.g., bay' with unknown subject matter).

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'aw' in creative speech gives a choice; in informative speech it may indicate doubt.

The particle 'aw' (أو) is a small word with big legal consequences. This passage from Nur al-Anwar analyzes its meaning, distinguishing between its role in insha' (declarations that create legal reality) and khabar (reports). Understanding this distinction is essential for interpreting statements like 'this slave or that is free' and for determining the validity of contracts where 'aw' introduces uncertainty. The Hanafi school takes a nuanced position: 'aw' in insha' gives a choice among alternatives, but it is not a sign of doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
State the Hanafi position: 'aw' in insha' statements (like freeing a slave or appointing an agent) is used for takhyir—giving a choice among the mentioned alternatives, so the ruling applies to any one of them.
The passage begins: 'And 'aw' is for one of the mentioned things.'
2
Refute the Doubt Interpretation
Understand why 'aw' is not for doubt in insha'. The passage argues that doubt is not the speaker's intent; if doubt were intended, the word 'shakk' would be used. Doubt can be a byproduct of the speech, but not the purpose.
The text says: 'doubt is not the speaker's intent but rather follows from the speech.'
3
Analyze the Dual Nature of the Statement
Recognize that such a statement combines aspects of insha' (creative, e.g., freeing one slave) and khabar (informative, reporting which slave is intended). This dual nature imposes conditions, e.g., the object (mahall) must exist at the time of declaration.
If one slave dies before specification, the speaker cannot retroactively claim the deceased was intended.
4
Apply to Wakalah
Note that using 'aw' in appointing an agent (tawkīl) is valid because tawkīl is insha', and 'aw' gives choice among the appointed agents. Each agent can act independently.
The passage explicitly says: 'When the particle 'aw' enters into wakalah, it is also valid.'
5
Identify the Invadility in Bay' and Ijarah, and the Istihsan Exception
Understand why 'aw' in sale/lease creates uncertainty (jahl) about the object or price, generally voiding the contract. However, by istihsan, if the person with the option (khyār) is known among two or three alternatives, using 'aw' for goods or price is valid—limited to three because they cover good, medium, bad qualities.
The exception shows Hanafi concern for avoiding gharar while accommodating trade flexibility.

Source Text

قوله : وأو لأحد المذكورين وقوله هذا حر او هذا كقولها هما حر و جعل البيان انشاء من وجه واخبار من وجه واذا دخلت فى الوكالة يصح بخلاف البيع والاجارة الا أن يكون من له الخيار معلوماً فى اثنين أو ثلاثة فيصح استحساناً۔ اور ( أو ) احد المذکورین کیلئے آتا ہے یعنی جن دو چیزوں کو (أو) کے ذریعے ذکر کیا گیا ہے حکم کو ان میں سے ایک کیلئے ثابت کرتا ہے۔ جیسے اگر کسی نے اپنے دو غلاموں کی طرف اشارہ کر کے کہا هذا حر أو هذا تو ان میں سے ایک آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ بعض علماء کہتے ہیں کہ ( أو ) کو شک کیلئے وضع کیا گیا ہے لیکن یہ بات صحیح نہیں اسلئے کہ شک متکلم کا مقصود نہیں ہوتا بلکہ حمل کلام سے لازم آتا ہے اور اگر شک مقصود بھی ہو تو اس کے لئے ( شک ) کا لفظ موجود ہے اور یہ کلام چونکہ انشاء کا بھی احتمال رکھتا ہے اور خبر کا بھی لہذا متکلم کی طرف سے تعین ضروری ہے ۔ کہ وہ بیان کرے کہ ان میں سے کون سا غلام مراد ہے۔ اور اس مقام پر متکلم کے بیان کو من وجہ انشاء اور من وجہ اخبار سمجھا جاتا ہے گویا کہ عنق اب پایا جارہا ہے۔ لہذا یہ شرط ہے کہ حمل محق کو قبول کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو تو اگر دونوں میں سے ایک غلام مر گیا اور پھر متکلم نے کہا کہ یہی غلام میری مراد تھا تو اس کی بات کو قبول نہیں کیا جائے گا اور چونکہ یہ من وجہ اخبار ہے لہذا قاضی اس کو غلام کے آزاد کرنے پر مجبور کر سکتا ہے۔ جب حرف ( أو ) وکالت پر داخل ہو تو بھی صحیح ہوگا اور ان دونوں وکیلوں میں سے ہر ایک کو تصرف کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا کیونکہ توکیل بھی انشاء ہے اور انشاء میں أو تخییر کیلئے ہوتا ہے، بخلاف بیع اور اجارہ کے کہ اس میں یہ نہیں کہہ سکتا بعت هذا أو هذا او اجرت هذا بالف او بالفین کیونکہ معقود علیہ اور معقود بہ مجہول رہ جائے گا لیکن اگر من له الخيار معلوم ہو تو دو یا تین مبیع اور ثمن میں أو کا لانا صحیح ہوگا لیکن اسے زیادہ میں صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ تین جید متوسط اور ردی پر
He said: And 'aw' is for one of the mentioned things. And his statement 'this is free or this' is like his saying 'both are free' and the statement is considered insha' from one aspect and khabar from another. And when it enters into wakalah it is valid, unlike bay' and ijarah, unless the one with the option is known among two or three, then it is valid by istihsan. And 'aw' comes for one of the mentioned things, meaning that it establishes the ruling for one of the two things mentioned with 'aw'. For example, if someone points to his two slaves and says 'this is free or this', then one of them becomes free. Some scholars say that 'aw' is placed for doubt, but this is not correct because doubt is not the speaker's intent but rather follows from the speech; and if doubt were intended, the word 'shakk' exists. And this speech because it has the possibility of being insha' and also khabar, therefore specification by the speaker is necessary. He must state which slave is intended. And in this context, the speaker's statement is considered insha' from one aspect and khabar from another, as if it is being realized immediately. Therefore it is a condition that the mahall (locus) has the capacity to accept the ruling. So if one of the two slaves dies and then the speaker says that this slave was my intent, his statement is not accepted. And because it is khabar from one aspect, the judge can compel him to free the slave. When the particle 'aw' enters into wakalah, it is also valid, and each of the two agents has the authority to act because tawkīl (appointment) is insha', and in insha' 'aw' is for takhyīr (choice). Unlike bay' and ijarah, where one cannot say 'I sold this or this' or 'I leased this for a thousand or two thousand' because the object of contract and the consideration remain unknown. But if the person with the option is known among two or three, then bringing 'aw' in the sold item or price is valid, but it is not valid in more than three because three encompass good, medium, and bad.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement from the matn (likely from Nur al-Anwar) regarding the particle 'aw' (أو). It first establishes the general rule: 'aw' is used to give a choice among the mentioned alternatives, applying the ruling to any one of them. The example of freeing one of two slaves illustrates that a declaration using 'aw' between two possible objects results in a binding obligation to free one — but which one is unspecified, requiring the speaker to clarify. The passage then refutes the claim that 'aw' indicates doubt, arguing that doubt is incidental and not the speaker's aim; if doubt were meant, the explicit word 'shakk' would be used. The legal nature of such a statement is analyzed: it combines aspects of insha' (creative/performative speech) because it creates a new legal situation, and khabar (informative speech) because it reports on the speaker's intent. Consequently, if one of the slaves dies before specification, the speaker cannot retrospectively claim that the deceased was the intended one, as the speech is treated partly as a report that must refer to an existing object. The qadi can enforce the freeing of the surviving slave. The passage then applies this to wakalah: using 'aw' in appointing agents is valid because tawkīl is insha', where 'aw' grants choice to the appointing party that any of the named agents may act. In contrast, in bay' (sale) and ijarah (lease), 'aw' creates uncertainty about the object (ma'qud 'alayh) or price (ma'qud bih), rendering the contract void. An exception exists by istihsan: if the person with the option (e.g., in a khyār condition) is explicitly known among two or three alternatives, then using 'aw' for the goods or price is valid. This is limited to two or three because these numbers cover a manageable range of qualities (good, medium, bad). The commentary follows the Hanafi school's principles of contractual clarity and the aversion to gharar (uncertainty).

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle indicating takhyir (choice) among alternatives, used in insha' statements to give a choice of one of the mentioned items.
انشاء (insha'): A speech act that creates a legal reality, such as contracts, divorces, or manumissions.
خبر (khabar): A speech act that reports on an existing state of affairs, which may be true or false.
تخییر (takhyir): Giving a choice between alternatives; here, the legal effect of aw in insha'.
محل (mahall): The locus or subject matter to which the ruling applies; it must exist for the statement to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, why is using 'aw' in a sale contract (bay') generally invalid?
A) Because 'aw' indicates doubt and doubt invalidates contracts.
B) Because it creates uncertainty (jahl) about the object or price, leading to gharar.
C) Because 'aw' is only valid in insha' statements like divorce or manumission.
D) Because the Hanafi school forbids any use of 'aw' in financial transactions.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'aw' in creative declarations (insha') gives a choice among the mentioned alternatives, but it is invalid in sale/lease unless the option is confined to a known set of two or three.

Meanings of 'Aw' in Hanafi Usul: Real and Metaphorical Uses
Explaining real and metaphorical uses of 'aw'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the real and metaphorical meanings of the letter 'aw' (أو) in Hanafi usul, apply the principle of contextual interpretation to differentiate between takhyir (choice) and tab'ad (distribution), and evaluate the ikhtilaf with Imam Malik regarding Quran 5:33.

Core Idea
The letter 'aw' is real for choice, but metaphorically means distribution when context demands — a qarina shifts its meaning.

This passage from Khulasat al-Anwar explains the Hanafi position on the letter 'aw'. While its real meaning is choice between alternatives, Shari'ah contexts often require a distributive reading. Understanding when 'aw' is real versus metaphorical is essential for correct istinbat — extracting legal rulings from texts. This lesson will unpack the Hanafi method of contextual interpretation, using mahr, kaffarah, and the bandit verse as examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the real (haqiqi) meaning of 'aw'
According to Hanafi usul, the real meaning of the letter 'aw' is takhyir (choice), indicating that the obligated person may choose any one of the alternatives.
This is the default unless a qarina redirects it.
2
Recognize when 'aw' takes a metaphorical meaning
When a qarina (contextual indicator) is present, 'aw' shifts to a metaphorical meaning such as tab'ad (distribution) or ibaha (permissibility).
The qarina can be textual, logical, or circumstantial.
3
Analyze the examples from the passage
The passage provides examples: mahr (choice beneficial), kaffarah (choice among alternatives), and the bandit verse (distribution by crime type).
In mahr, 'aw' is real choice; in bandit verse, it is metaphorical distribution.
4
Compare the Hanafi and Maliki positions on the bandit verse
Imam Malik holds 'aw' as real choice; Hanafis argue it means 'bal' (rather) due to the hadith and logical necessity.
The difference leads to different rulings: fixed punishment per crime vs. judge's discretion.
5
Derive the usul principle
The Hanafi principle: al-haqiqah tu'khadhu bi qarinatiha (the real meaning is taken with its context). Hence, 'aw' is only interpreted as choice when no qarina exists.
This principle governs many usul discussions.

It includes. His saying: And in the mahr likewise according to them (the two disciples) if the choice is valid. And in the two currencies, the lesser is obligatory. And according to him (Abu Hanifa), the mahr of the like is obligatory if the mahr of the like is two thousand. And in the expiation, one of the two things is obligatory, contrary to some. According to the two disciples, in mahr also, bringing the letter 'aw' is correct when there is a benefit in choice, i.e., benefit for one and loss for the other. And if there is no benefit in choice, then [takhayyur?] and [kathir?] and of the two currencies, the lesser becomes obligatory, like one thousand and two thousand, and [fa'f'al?] example: one thousand cash and two thousand deferred. According to Imam Sahib, in these cases, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, but if one thousand cash and two thousand deferred, then if mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the woman has choice; if mahr al-mithl is one thousand or less, the man has choice. Every expiation in which the letter 'aw' is brought between several things, there is choice, and only one thing is obligatory, like the expiation of a vow, head shaving, etc. And if he performs all the things between which there was choice, then the expiation is fulfilled by one thing only; the rest are not performed as expiation but as voluntary charity. And if he does not perform any of these things, then punishment is for only one due to non-performance, but according to some, all these things are obligatory alternatively, meaning if he performs one, the obligation falls; if he performs none, punishment is for not performing all. We say: your statement is against [ahkam?] and the occasion of Shari'ah, therefore it is not accepted.
His saying: And in His saying 'that they be killed or crucified' for choice according to Imam Malik, and according to us it means 'rather': they are killed if they killed only, rather they are crucified if the highway robbery involved killing or taking money, rather their hands and feet are cut off if they took money only, rather they are exiled from the land if they frightened the road.
The metaphorical meaning of 'aw'.
After explaining the real meaning of 'aw', the author explains its metaphorical meaning. He writes that in the verse 'that they be killed or crucified', according to Imam Malik, 'aw' indicates choice, while according to us it does not indicate choice but has the meaning of 'bal' (rather), because the crimes of bandits are of four types: (1) only taking money, (3) killing and taking money, (2) only killing, (4) only threatening. So their punishments are also four: if the crime is severe, punishment is severe; if light, punishment is light. Basically, this detail also comes in hadith, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) made a treaty with Abu Barza, then some of his companions violated the treaty and robbed some people coming with the intention of Islam, so Jibreel (peace be upon him) brought down a ruling from Allah: he who killed and took money should be crucified, he who killed but did not take money should be killed, he who took money but did not kill should have his hands and feet cut off, and he who only threatened should be exiled. But Imam Sahib says that crucifixion is included with taking money and killing, but this
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the usul principle regarding the letter 'aw' (or). It begins by stating that the passage includes the rule: in mahr (dower), according to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), bringing 'aw' is valid if choice is beneficial. In the case of two currencies (cash vs. deferred), the lesser amount is obligatory according to them. According to Abu Hanifa, mahr al-mithl (proper dower) is obligatory if it is two thousand. The commentary then explains in Urdu: according to the two disciples, 'aw' in mahr is correct when there is benefit in choice; otherwise, the lesser amount is wajib. For example, one thousand cash vs. two thousand deferred: if mahr al-mithl is two thousand or more, the woman chooses; if less, the man chooses. Next, in kaffarah (expiation), 'aw' indicates choice; only one thing is needed. If all are performed, only one counts as kaffarah; the rest are voluntary. If none are performed, punishment is for one, but some say all are alternative obligations. The commentator rejects a contrary view as against Shari'ah. Then the metaphorical meaning of 'aw' is explained with the verse on bandits (Quran 5:33). Imam Malik holds 'aw' indicates choice among punishments. Hanafis say it means 'bal' (rather), distributing punishments according to the crime. This is supported by a hadith about the incident of Abu Barza. Imam Abu Hanifa includes crucifixion with killing and taking money. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of interpreting 'aw' contextually: real meaning is choice, but metaphorical meaning (as in the verse) is distribution or alternation based on the maqam (context).

Key Terms
أو (aw): The letter 'or' used for choice (takhyir) in its real meaning, and for distribution (tab'ad) or alternation (bil ma'na) metaphorically when a qarina exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to Hanafi usul, what is the real (haqiqi) meaning of the letter 'أو' (aw)?
A) Presenting alternatives without preference
B) Choice (takhyir)
C) Distribution (tab'ad)
D) Cumulative (both must be done)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'aw' is real for choice but metaphorical for distribution when a qarina is present — a key principle of contextual interpretation.

When literal meaning is impossible: can majaz save the statement?
Analyzing the dispute on majaz when haqiqah is impossible

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the underlying usul principle in the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on using majaz when haqiqah is impossible, and evaluate both arguments.

Core Idea
If literal meaning is impossible, Abu Hanifa permits metaphorical interpretation to avoid nullification; the Sahibayn reject this.

In Hanafi usul, when a statement's literal meaning is impossible due to logical or practical constraints, a dispute arises: can we resort to metaphorical interpretation (majaz) to salvage the utterance? This lesson examines a case where a master says to his slave and his animal 'this is free or this' (هذا حر أو هذا). The Sahibayn rule the statement void; Imam Abu Hanifa argues that metaphorical interpretation is possible, forcing the speaker to specify. We'll analyze their proofs and the underlying usul principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the exact wording of the master's statement: 'هذا حر أو هذا' addressed to a slave and an animal. The literal meaning is impossible because 'this' is unspecified and the animal cannot be freed.
2
Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn say the statement is invalid (باطل) because the literal meaning is impossible and no specification exists. They deny the permissibility of metaphorical interpretation when the literal meaning is impossible.
They rely on the principle that if haqiqah is impossible, no valid meaning remains.
3
Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Imam Abu Hanifa agrees that literarily it is unspecified, but he allows metaphorical interpretation (majaz) that gives a probability of specification. He analogizes with the case of two slaves where specification is required. The principle: 'العمل بالمحتمل أولى من الإهدار' (acting on the probable is better than nullification).
4
Trace the underlying usul dispute
The core disagreement is whether majaz can be employed when the literal meaning is impossible. Abu Hanifa says yes, to save the speaker's intent; the Sahibayn say no, because without a valid literal meaning, metaphor has no foundation.
5
Determine the practical consequence
According to Abu Hanifa's view, the speaker must specify which one he meant (ta'yin). According to the Sahibayn, the statement is void and no emancipation occurs at all.
This difference affects legal outcomes in declarations of emancipation and similar ambiguous utterances.

قوله : وقا لا اذا قال لعبده ودابته هذا حر أو هذا انه با طل لأنه اسم لأحدهما غير عين وذالك غير محل للعتق وعنده هو كذلك لكن على احتمال التعين حتى لزمه التعيين كما في مسألة العبدين والعمل بالمحتمل أولى من الاهدار وهما ينكر ان الاستعارة عند استحالة الحكم فهما جريا . صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنے نام اور چوپائے کو کہا هذا حر أو هذا تو یہ کلام باطل ہوگا اسلئے کہ خدا کا مشار الیہ ان میں سے کسی غیر معین کو بنایا گیا ہے اور غیر معین محق کا محل نہیں بن سکتا، جبکہ امام صاحب کہتے ہیں کہ اگر چہ حقیقتا تو ایسے ہی ہے لیکن مجازا یہ تعین کا احتمال رکھتا ہے بند متکلم پرتعیین لازم ہوگی اصل میں یہ اختلاف اس اختلاف پر مبنی ہے کہ اگر حقیقت محال ہو تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک مجاز مراد لے سکتے ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں مجاز مراد نہیں لے سکتے ۔
He said: And they both said: When he says to his slave and his animal 'this is free or this', it is invalid because it is a name for one of them unspecified, and that is not a locus for freeing. And according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is likewise, but it has the probability of specification, so specification is necessary from the speaker, as in the case of two slaves, and acting on the probable is better than nullifying. And they both deny that metaphorical usage is permissible when the literal meaning is impossible, thus they proceeded. Then Urdu: The Sahibayn say that if a person says to his slave and his animal 'this is free or this', this statement is invalid because the referent (mushtar ilayh) is made from among them unspecified, and an unspecified thing cannot be the locus of freeing. Whereas Imam Abu Hanifa says that although literally it is so, metaphorically it has the probability of specification, so specification is necessary for the speaker. Originally, this dispute is based on the disagreement that if the literal meaning is impossible, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is permissible to take the metaphorical meaning, whereas in that case the Sahibayn do not take the metaphorical meaning.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) regarding the interpretation of the word 'أو' when used in a declaration of emancipation. The scenario: a master says to his slave and his animal 'هذا حر أو هذا' (this is free or this). Literally, 'هذا' refers to one of them unspecified, but since one is a slave and the other is not (the animal cannot be freed), the literal meaning is impossible. The Sahibayn argue that because the literal meaning is impossible and no specific referent is determined, the statement is void. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, allows a metaphorical interpretation: 'أو' can imply a probability of specification, forcing the speaker to make a definite decision (ta'yin). This is supported by a similar case involving two slaves. The underlying usul principle is whether majaz (metaphor) can be used when haqiqah (literal meaning) is impossible. Imam Abu Hanifa permits it, while the Sahibayn do not. This reflects a broader Hanafi tendency to preserve the validity of speech through metaphorical interpretation rather than declaring it void.

Key Terms
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical or figurative meaning of a word, used when the literal meaning is impossible or unlikely.
استحالة الحقيقة (istihalat al-haqiqah): The impossibility of the literal meaning due to logical or practical constraints.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The statement is valid and both are freed.
B) The statement is invalid because literal interpretation is impossible.
C) The speaker must specify immediately.
D) The animal is freed.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of majaz when haqiqah is impossible depends on whether one prioritizes saving the speech act (Abu Hanifa) or rejecting it due to impossibility (Sahibayn).
