Kam as a Noun for Number: A Usul Definition
Defining 'kam' as a noun for number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'kam' as a noun for number and apply its usul definition to determine that a divorce conditional upon 'kam' does not occur until the wife wishes.

Core Idea
Kam is a noun for an unspecified number, making a divorce conditional on the wife's wish.

This lesson examines the usul definition of 'kam' as a noun denoting an unspecified number. The matn clarifies its grammatical category and then applies it to a divorce scenario: if a husband says 'you are divorced kam ma shi'ta', the divorce is suspended until the wife actually wishes. Understanding this definition is key to grasping how conditional language operates in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify grammatical status
Recognize that 'kam' is an ism (noun), not a harf (particle) or fi'l (verb). This determines its function in conditional phrases.
Hanafi usul treats 'kam' as a noun, which is crucial for its legal effect.
2
Understand 'number that occurs'
'Al-ʿadad al-wāqiʿ' means an actual but unspecified quantity. 'Kam' does not specify a number; it implies an unstated amount.
This distinguishes it from explicit numbers like 'thalaatha' (three).
3
Apply to divorce context
When a husband says 'anti taliq kam ma shi't', the divorce is suspended until the wife wishes. Because 'kam' is unspecified, the number of divorces is contingent on her will.
The divorce does not take effect until she exercises her wish.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وكم اسم للعدد الواقع فاذا قال انت طالق كم شئت لم تطلق مالم تشاء . (کم) عدد واقع کا اسم ہے لہذا اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا انت طالق کم شئت تو جب تک وہ نہیں چاہئے کی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔
His saying: And 'kam' is a noun for the number that occurs. If he says 'you are divorced kam ma shi'ta', she is not divorced unless she wishes. (Kam) is a noun for the number that occurs. Therefore if someone says to his wife 'anti taliq kama shi't', the divorce is not effective until she wishes.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This is a definitional lesson from the matn. The word 'kam' (as much as) is categorized as a noun (ism) that denotes an unspecified number. When used in the divorce phrase, it suspends the occurrence of divorce on the wife's wish. The commentator explains that until she actually wishes, no divorce takes place. This is a straightforward linguistic rule in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
كم (kam): A noun for number, indicating an unspecified amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the grammatical status of 'kam' in the phrase 'anti taliq kama shi't'?
A) It is a verb
B) It is a particle
C) It is a noun for number
D) It is a proper noun

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'kam' is a noun for an unspecified number, making any conditional statement that uses it dependent on the implied wish.

The Hanafi Rule of Taghlib: Masculine Plural Includes Females in Mixed Contexts
Hanafi rule with Shafi'i opposition and application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of taghlib to determine whether a masculine plural term includes females in mixed contexts, and contrast the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on this linguistic principle.

Core Idea
The masculine plural in mixed contexts includes both genders by taghlib, unless context is purely female.

This passage from Nur al-Anwar introduces a foundational linguistic rule in Hanafi usul: when a masculine plural form is used in a context where both males and females are present, it includes both, by way of predominance (taghlib). The Hanafi school relies on this principle to interpret legal texts, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds a differing view. Understanding this dispute is key to grasping how the Hanafi school approaches gender-inclusive language in the Quran and legal documents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
State the Hanafi rule: the masculine plural with the sign of masculinity includes both males and females when the context is mixed, but does not include females when they are alone. Conversely, the feminine plural includes only females.
The rule is limited to mixed contexts; when only females are present, the masculine plural does not apply.
2
Locate the evidential basis
Find the Hanafi proof: Quran 2:228 'For men is a degree over them' (الرجال عليهن درجة) which indicates male predominance, justifying the inclusion of females under the masculine plural.
This is a zanni dalala (probative indication) for the rule.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that if the masculine plural included females, phrases like 'al-muslimin wa al-muslimat' (the Muslim men and the Muslim women) would be redundant, because the first term would already include women.
Redundancy (takrār) is considered undesirable in eloquent speech.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that such explicit mention of both is for emphasis and to please the hearts of the female companions, not to indicate exclusion. It does not negate the default rule of taghlib.
The response addresses the redundancy objection by providing a valid rhetorical purpose.
5
Apply the rule to a legal example
From al-Siyar al-Kabir: If someone says 'grant aman to my sons (banī)' and he has both sons and daughters, the aman includes both. If he says 'my daughters (banātī)', it excludes sons. If he says 'my sons' but only has daughters, the aman does not include them.
The example illustrates the boundary conditions: taghlib works when both genders are present, not when only females exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : الجمع المذكر بعلامة الذكور عندنا يتناول الذكور والاناث عند الاختلاط ولا يتناول الاناث المفردات وان ذكر بعلامة التانيث يتناول الاناث خاصة . اس کے بعد مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ جمع مذکر جس میں ذکور کی علامت ہو اور اختلاط کے وقت ذکور اور اناث دونوں کو تغیلبہ شامل ہوتی ہے لیکن اس سے برعکس نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ مردوں کو عورتوں پر غلبہ ہے کما قال الله تعالی للرجال عليهن درجة : کہ عورتوں کو مردوں پر ۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اختلاط کے وقت بھی اناث کو شامل نہیں ہوگی ورنہ ان المسلمين والمسلمات میں تکرار لازم آئے گا۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ تو صرف ان صحابیات کے دل کو خوش کرنے کے لئے ہے لھذا اگر جمع مؤنث کی علامت کے ساتھ ہو تو وہ صرف اناث کو شامل ہوگی۔ قوله : حتى قال في السير الكبير اذاقال امنوني على بنى وله بنون وبنات ان الامان يتناول الفريقين ولو قال آمنو ني على بناتى لا يتناول الذكور من اولاده ولو قال على بني وليس له سوى البنات لا يثبت الامان لهن۔
His saying: The masculine plural with the sign of masculinity, according to us, includes males and females when mixed, and does not include females alone. And if it is mentioned with the sign of femininity, it includes only females. Thereafter, the author says: The masculine plural that has the sign of masculinity, and at the time of mixing, includes both males and females by way of predominance (taghlib), but not the reverse, because males have predominance over females, as Allah said: 'For men is a degree over them' (2:228). Imam al-Shafi'i says that even when mixed, it does not include females, otherwise there would be redundancy in 'muslimin and muslimat'. We say that this is only to please the hearts of those female companions. Therefore if it is with the sign of femininity, it includes only females. His saying: Until he said in al-Siyar al-Kabir: If someone says 'grant aman to my sons' and he has sons and daughters, the aman includes both groups. If he says 'grant aman to my daughters', it does not include male children. If he says 'my sons' and he only has daughters, aman is not established for them.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage establishes a linguistic rule in Hanafi usul: when a masculine plural (with masculine ending) is used in a context where both males and females are present, it includes females by way of taghlib (predominance). This is based on the principle that males have a degree over females (Quran 2:228). Imam al-Shafi'i opposes this, arguing that if the masculine plural included females, then phrases like 'al-muslimin wa al-muslimat' would be redundant. The Hanafi response is that such explicit mention of both is for emphasis and to please the female companions, not to indicate exclusion. The rule is applied in practical fatawa, as illustrated by the example from al-Siyar al-Kabir: the word 'bani' (my sons) includes daughters if he has both, but 'banati' (my daughters) excludes sons. If he only has daughters, 'bani' does not refer to them.

Key Terms
تغیلبہ (taghlib): Predominance; the linguistic principle of including the less dominant gender under the masculine plural.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man says 'grant security to my sons' and he has both sons and daughters, who is included?
A) Only sons
B) Only daughters
C) Both sons and daughters
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule of taghlib holds that a masculine plural term in a mixed context includes females, but when only females exist, the term does not include them.

The Scope of Masculine Plural (Jami' Mudhakkar) by Taghlib
Debate on inclusive scope of masculine plural by taghlib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on inclusive masculine plural and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument regarding redundancy.

Core Idea
The masculine plural includes females by taghlib due to male dominance; the feminine plural excludes males.

This passage addresses a fundamental usul al-fiqh dispute: does the masculine plural form (like 'muslimina') include women when both genders are present? The Hanafi school, relying on taghlib and Quranic usage, says yes. Imam al-Shafi'i objects that if it included women, then explicit pairing like 'muslimina wa muslimati' would be redundant. The Hanafi reply: such pairing is for reassurance, not necessity. The practical impact is seen in legal documents, such as grants of aman (security).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate that the masculine plural with masculine sign includes both males and females by taghlib when intermixing occurs.
Takes from the text: 'جمع مذکر جس میں ذکور کی علامت ہو اور اختلاط کے وقت ذکور اور اناث دونوں کو تغیلیباً شامل ہوتی ہے'
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that if the masculine plural included females, there would be no need for separate feminine forms, making expressions like 'al-muslimina wa al-muslimati' redundant.
The text uses 'المسلمين والمسلمات' as an example.
3
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that such dual mention is only for pleasing hearts and emphasis, not a logical necessity. The dominance of males (taghlib) is derived from Quranic verse (2:228) and common usage.
The verse 'للرجال عليهن درجة' is cited as support.
4
Apply to the example from al-Siyar al-Kabir
Examine the three cases: 1) 'bani' with both sons and daughters includes both; 2) 'banati' excludes sons; 3) 'bani' when only daughters exist does not include them.
This illustrates the practical rule in a legal document context.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: in grants of security, contracts, or general legal phrasing, the Hanafi school includes females under masculine plural while the Shafi'i school does not unless specified.
This affects interpretation of wills, waqf, and other documents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس کے بعد مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ جمع مذکر جس میں ذکور کی علامت ہو اور اختلاط کے وقت ذکور اور اناث دونوں کو تغیلبہ شامل ہوتی ہے لیکن اس سے برعکس نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ مردوں کو عورتوں پر غلبہ حاصل ہے کما قال الله تعالی للرجال عليهن درجة : کہ عورتوں کو مردوں پر ۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اختلاط کے وقت بھی اناث کو شامل نہیں ہوگی ورنہ ان المسلمين والمسلمات میں تکرار لازم آئے گا۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ تو صرف ان صحابیات کے دل کو خوش کرنے کے لئے ہے لھذا اگر جمع مؤنث کی علامت کے ساتھ ہو تو وہ صرف اناث کو شامل ہوگی۔ قوله : حتى قال في السير الكبير اذاقال امنوني على بنى وله بنون وبنات ان الامان يتناول الفريقين ولو قال آمنو ني على بناتى لا يتناول الذكور من اولاده ولو قال على بني وليس له سوى البنات لا يثبت الامان لهن.
Then the author says: That masculine plural which has the sign of masculinity and at the time of intermixing includes both males and females by taghlib, but the opposite does not happen because men have dominance over women, as Allah Almighty said: 'For men is a degree over them.' Imam Shafi'i says that even at the time of intermixing it does not include females, otherwise in 'al-muslimina wa al-muslimati' there would be repetition. We say that this is only to please the hearts of those female companions. Therefore if the plural is with the feminine sign, it includes only females. His statement: Even said in al-Siyar al-Kabir: If he says 'grant security to my sons' and he has sons and daughters, the security includes both groups. If he says 'grant security to my daughters', it does not include the male children. If he says 'to my sons' and he has only daughters, the security is not established for them.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage discusses a usul al-fiqh dispute regarding the scope of the masculine plural when males and females are mixed. The Hanafi position is that the masculine plural (with the masculine marker) includes females by way of taghlib (overwhelming inclusion) because of the inherent dominance of males, citing Quran 2:228. Imam Shafi'i objects that if the masculine plural included females, then expressions like 'al-muslimina wa al-muslimati' would be redundant. The Hanafi response is that such explicit mention of both is only for reassurance, not for necessity. The passage then provides a practical example from al-Siyar al-Kabir: when a man says 'grant security to my sons' and he has both sons and daughters, the security covers all children because the masculine plural includes females by taghlib. But if he says 'grant security to my daughters', it excludes sons. And if he has only daughters but says 'my sons', the security is invalid since the phrase does not apply. This illustrates the rule: the masculine plural with masculine sign includes females when mixed, but the feminine plural is exclusive.

Key Terms
تغیلیب (taghlib): Overwhelming inclusion of females under masculine plural due to male dominance
جمع مذکر (jami' mudhakkar): Masculine plural form with letter of masculinity

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The daughters are included because masculine plural is general.
B) The daughters are not included because the masculine plural only refers to males.
C) The daughters are included only if he also has sons.
D) The daughters are excluded because the phrase is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts taghlib: the masculine plural with masculine sign includes females when mixed, but the feminine plural excludes males.

Kinayah: Definition, Ruling, and Application in Divorce
Definition, ruling, and application of kinayah in divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define kinayah according to Hanafi usul, state its ruling (action not obligatory without intention), and apply this to classify divorce utterances as kinayah or sarih and determine the legal outcome.

Core Idea
Kinayah requires intention for legal effect; ambiguity in the referent makes it kinayah, not sarih.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not every utterance is legally explicit. Some words, called kinayah, have a hidden intended meaning that becomes clear only through a contextual clue (qarina) or the speaker's intention (niyyah). This lesson explains how the commentators of Noor al-Anwar define kinayah, its governing rule, and how it applies to divorce words like 'anti ba'in'. Understanding this distinction is crucial for deriving correct legal rulings in marriage and divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of kinayah
Locate the Arabic definition: 'ma istutira al-murad bihi wa la yufham illa bi qarinah'. Note that kinayah includes both haqiqah and majaz – the hiddenness is in the intended meaning, not the word itself.
The example given is pronouns (alifaz al-damir), which are context-dependent.
2
Extract the legal ruling (hukm) of kinayah
The passage states: 'an la yajiba al-amal biha illa bi al-niyyah'. This means acting upon a kinayah is not wajib (obligatory) until intention is present. For example, in divorce, a kinayah utterance does not effect divorce unless the husband intends divorce.
This distinguishes kinayah from sarih (explicit) words, which effect divorce even without intention.
3
Analyze the objection and response about divorce kinayah
An objection claims that words like 'anti ba'in' have known lexical meanings, so they cannot be kinayah. The response explains that although 'bain' means separation, it is unknown from what (husband, family, wealth, etc.). Hence intention is needed to specify the referent.
The response shows how the Hanafi usul principle of requiring clarity in the intended meaning is applied.
4
Distinguish between bayan scholars and usul scholars on kinayah status
The passage notes that according to bayan (rhetoric) scholars, these words are kinayah because they involve transferring from a necessary implication (e.g., 'long-necked' for tall). Usul scholars classify them differently, but Hanafi fiqh still requires intention for legal effect.
This illustrates an intra-disciplinary nuance: the same term may have different definitions in different disciplines.
5
Apply the ruling to exceptions: 'i'taddi', 'istabri'i rahimaki', 'anti wahidah'
These kinayah words produce a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) because the word 'talaq' is implied. For example, 'i'taddi' means 'observe your waiting period', which implies a preceding divorce. No separate intention for divorce is needed beyond the contextual implication.
This shows that even within kinayah, the presence of a qarina (like the implied word 'talaq') can change the ruling from requiring intention to being effective directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله :
وأما الكناية فما استتر المراد به
ولا يفهم الا بقرينة حقيقة كان أو مجاز أ مثل الفاظ
الضمير وحكمها أن لا يجب العمل بها الا با لنية .

حقیقت ہو یا مجاز ۔ کنایہ میں جو پوشیدگی ہوتی ہے وہ استعمال کے اعتبارت ہوتی ہے جیسے کہ الفاظ ضمیر ہیں، انسا ، و انت وغیرہ یہ سب اس لئے وضع کئے گئے ہیں تا کہ ان کو متکلم خفاء کے طور پر

باقی نحویوں کے ہاں ضمیر کا اعرف المعارف ہونا ضروری بات ہے

اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اس پر عمل کر ن اس وقت تک واجب نہیں جب تک اس کے کسی معنی
کی تربیت نہ ہو یا نسیت کے قائم مقام کوئی اور چیز نہ ہو۔
قوله : وكنايات الطلاق يت بها مجازاً حتى كانت بو
ائن .
ایک اہم اعتراض کا دفعیہ :
اعتراض : کنایه تو ده و تابے بس کی باشید درون لانك انت بائن ، بتة بتلة،
حرام دان رام و غیر وان سب کے معانی تو معلوم ہیں۔ جواب ان الفاظ کو ان یہ کہتا جا تا ہے ۔ کیونکہ مالی بائن کا من ناح کیے۔ معلوم ہے یعنی جدا ہونا کو کن یہ شالا صبح
لیکن یہ معلوم نہیں کہ کس چیز سے جدا ہے شوہر سے ، خاندان سے، مال سے یا جمال سے تو جب
شوہر نے نیت کر لی کہ یہ مجھ سے جدا ہے تو طلاق بائن واقع ہو جائے گی ۔
کنا یہ وہ ہوتا ہے جس کا لغوی معنی معلوم ہو لیکن معنی مرادی پوشیدہ ہو اور یہ الفاظ بھی اسی طرح ہیں لہذا یہ کنایہ ہونے چاہئیں اس لئے بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے یہ علمائے بیان کے مذہب کے مطابق
کنایات ہیں ۔ اور علمائے اصول کے مذہب کے مطابق یہ کنایات میں سے نہیں ہیں لیکن علمائے بیان کے نزدیک کنا یہ وہ ہوتا ہے کہ لفظ کو ذکر کیا جائے اور اس کا معنی موضوع لہ مراد لیا جائے لیکن اس کی ذات کی حیثیت سے نہیں بلکہ اس حیثیت سستے کہ لازم معنی سے اس کے مزدم کی طرف انتقال
کیا جائے جیسے طویل النجاد .
قوله : الا اعتدى واستبر ئي رحمك وأنت واحدة لیکن اعتدى ، و استبر ئي رحمك ، وانت واحدة من الفاظ ایسے ہیں کہ دائی ہونے کے باوجود ان سے طلاق رجعی واقع ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ ان الفاظ میں
لفظ طلاق تقدیر ا موجود ہے مثلاً اعتدی میں اللہ کی نعمتوں کو شمار کرنے کا بھی احتمال ہے اور عدت سے فارغ ہو

ی ہوگی انت طالق فاستبرئي رحمك .
اب رها انت واحدة اس میں یہ بھی احتمال تے کہ تو مال کے اعتبارت یہاں کے برها مال
[He said:] As for kinayah, it is that whose meaning is hidden and not understood except with a contextual clue (qarina), whether it is haqiqah or majaz, like the words of pronouns. Its ruling is that action upon it is not obligatory except with intention. Definition of kinayah: Kinayah is a word whose intended meaning is hidden and cannot be understood without a contextual clue, whether it is haqiqah or majaz. The hiddenness in kinayah comes from usage, such as the pronouns 'ana' and 'anta' etc., which are created to be used by the speaker in a hidden manner. As for grammarians, a pronoun is the most definite of known things. The ruling of kinayah: Its ruling is that acting upon it is not obligatory until its meaning is intended or something else takes its place. He said: Kinayah of divorce are used metaphorically such that they result in khul'? [The objection: Some say these words have known meanings. The answer: bain? means separation, but it is unknown from what? wife, family, wealth, etc. So when the husband intends 'she is separated from me', a irrevocable divorce occurs. Kinayah is that whose lexical meaning is known but intended meaning is hidden, and these words are like that. So some say according to the scholars of bayan they are kinayah, but according to usul scholars they are not. According to bayan scholars, kinayah is that a word is mentioned and its literal meaning is intended, but not in terms of its essence, rather as transferring from the necessary meaning to the intended, like 'tawil al-nijad'. He said: Except 'i'taddi', 'istabri'i rahimaki', and 'anti wahidah'. These words, despite being kinayah, produce a revocable divorce because in them the word 'talaq' is implied. For example, in 'i'taddi', there is a possibility of counting blessings or counting menstrual periods for completing the waiting period. When the intention is for menstruation, revocable divorce occurs, as if he mentioned the consequence and intended the cause, so the phrase is 'anti taliq fa'taddi'. Similarly, in 'istabri'i', there is possibility of seeking prayer? or mercy for children or for second marriage. When the intention is for second marriage, revocable divorce occurs, being 'anti taliq fastabri'i rahimaki'. As for 'anti wahidah', there is also a possibility that you are one in terms of wealth? [incomplete]
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Noor al-Anwar explains the concept of kinayah (indirect speech) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, specifically in the context of divorce. The author begins by quoting the original matn's definition: kinayah is a word whose intended meaning is hidden and requires a contextual clue (qarina) to be understood, regardless of whether the word is used in its literal (haqiqah) or metaphorical (majaz) sense. The example given is pronouns like 'I' and 'you' which are inherently hidden—their referent depends on context. The ruling is that no legal effect is produced from kinayah unless the speaker intends a specific meaning (i.e., has niyyah). This is a key distinction from sarih (explicit) speech. The discussion then turns to divorce kinayah words, such as 'anti ba'in' (you are separated), 'battah', 'battah', 'haram', etc. An objection is raised: these words have known lexical meanings, so how can they be kinayah? The answer: although the general meaning of separation is known, it is unclear from what—husband, family, wealth, or beauty? Thus, when the husband intends separation from his wife, an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) occurs. The author then notes that according to scholars of bayan (rhetoric), these words are considered kinayah because they involve transferring from a necessary implication to the intended meaning (like saying 'long-necked' for a tall person). However, usul scholars classify them differently because the mechanism differs from linguistic kinayah. The passage concludes with exceptions: the words 'i'taddi' (observe your waiting period), 'istabri'i rahimaki' (verify your womb is free), and 'anti wahidah' (you are one) are kinayah but produce a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) because the word 'talaq' is implied in the context. The explanation shows how Hanafi usul applies the concept of niyyah and qarina to determine the legal outcome of indirect speech.

Key Terms
كنایہ (kināyah): A word whose intended meaning is hidden and requires a contextual clue (qarina) to be understood, regardless of being haqiqah or majaz.
قرینہ (qarīnah): A contextual clue that reveals the intended meaning of a kinayah.
نیہ (niyyah): Intention, which is necessary for kinayah to have legal effect (e.g., divorce).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the divorce words 'i'taddi', 'istabri'i rahimaki', and 'anti wahidah' produce a revocable divorce despite being kinayah?
A) Because they are sarih (explicit) divorce words.
B) Because the word 'talaq' is implied in their context, serving as a qarina that makes them effective immediately.
C) Because they are considered majaz and thus always effect divorce regardless of intention.
D) Because they are exceptions that require intention but produce revocable divorce anyway.

Key Takeaway
Kinayah requires intention for legal effect; the hiddenness of the intended meaning (not the lexical meaning) determines its classification.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Distinguishing Isharat al-Nass from Ibarat al-Nass in Hanafi Usul
Defining isharat al-nass with exclusions and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define isharat al-nass, identify its three conditions, and distinguish it from ibarat al-nass and iqtida' al-nass using the Hanafi usul framework.

Core Idea
Isharat al-nass: the unintended linguistic implication of a text, binding but subordinate to ibara.

In Hanafi usul, the derivation of rulings from a text is not limited to its explicit meaning. There are layers: ibarat al-nass (explicit intent), isharat al-nass (linguistic implication not intended), and iqtida' al-nass (rational inference). This lesson unpacks the definition of isharat al-nass as given in Nur al-Anwar and its commentary, clarifying its conditions and how it operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
Deconstruct the definition
Break down the definition: 'acting upon what is established by its wording linguistically, but it is not intended nor was the speech brought for it, and it is not apparent from every angle.' Identify each restriction.
Focus on the three exclusions: lughatan vs. iqtida', ghayru maqsud vs. ibara, and laysa bi-zahirin min kulli wajh.
2
Understand the exclusions
Explain why each restriction is necessary: (1) 'lughatan' excludes iqtida' al-nass (rational implication), (2) 'ghayru maqsud' excludes ibara, (3) 'laysa bi-zahirin' emphasizes that ishara is not as apparent as ibara.
The commentator notes that the third phrase is not a separate condition but an emphasis.
3
Apply the sensory analogy
Consider the sensory example: looking at a person with full intent (ibara) versus peripheral vision (ishara). See how both arise from the same act of looking but differ in intentionality.
This helps concretize the abstract categories.
4
Analyze the Qur'anic example
Apply the definition to the verse 'wa 'ala al-mawludi lahu rizquhunna wa kiswatuhunna' (2:233). The lam of ikhtisas indicates lineage goes to the father. This ruling is derived by ishara, not ibara, because the primary intent is provision and clothing.
The author of Nur al-Anwar points out that the lam indicates specification (ikhtisas), which linguistically implies the father's responsibility and lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اما الاستدلال باشارة النص اصطلاحی تعریف: فهو العمل بما ثبت بنظمه لغة لكنه غير مقصود ولا سيق له النص وليس بظاهر من كل وجه یعنی لغت کے اعتبار سے لفظ سے ہو نا ہوم ثابت ہو اس نے ا تد اال کرنا اس طور پر کہ یہ مقصود نہ ہو اور نہ ہی کلام اسکے لئے لایا گیا ہو نہ یہ من جميع الوجوظاہر ہو۔ فوائد قيود بنطمه : جنس ہے جس میں اشارہ اس کے ساتھ ساتھ عبارت اس بھی شامل ہے کیونکہ اشارة العص کی طرح عبارة النص کا تعلق بھی نس کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ ایسی قیود کی ضرورت ہے جن کی بنا پر تعریف اشار وائس کے لئے جامع او ا سکے ماسوا کے دخول سے مانع ہو جائے۔ (۱) لغة اس قید سے وہ معنی نکل گیا جو اقتضاء النص کے طور پر ثابت ہوتا ہے کیونکہ وہ با منبا رافت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اس کا منتھی کبھی کبھی عقل ہوا کرتی ہے ۔ (۲) لكنه غير مقصود ولا سبق له النص: اس قید سے مبارة انس خارج ہو گیا ۔ کیونکہ وہ متصور ہوتا ہے اور کالام اسی مقصد کے لئے لایا جاتا ہے۔ شاریخ کا خیال ہے کہ مائن کا قول ليس بظاہر من كل وجه قيد اخترازی نہیں بلکہ یہ زيادہ تاکید کا فائدہ دے رہا ہے۔ بالفاظ دیگر اس سے اشارہ ان کی وجہ تسمیہ معلوم ہوتی ہے کہ اسے اشارہ اس وجہ سے کہتے ہیں کہ یہ ظاہر نہیں نہ اص ہے۔
عبارة النص اور اشارة النص کی حسی مثال شارخ نے اس کی حسی مثال یہ نیا ہے کہ جب کوئی شخص دوسرے شخص کو بنظر غامیر اور مکمل مقصد و ارادوست دیکھتا ہے تو ساتھ ہی ساتھ کوشید چشم سے وہ اس کے دائیں بائیں کی چیزوں پر بھی نظر کرتا ہے اگر چہ یہ مقصود نہیں ہوتیں ۔ پس بالقصد داردو دیکھنا عبارة النص اور بقیہ اشارۃ النص ہے۔ اشارة النص کی مثال: اللہ تعالی کا فرمان ہے وعلى المولود له رزقهن وكسوتهن . صاحب نور الانور فرماتے ہیں کہ انسولود لہ میں لام برائے اختصاص ہے، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچوں کا نسب ان کے باپ کی طرف سے چلے گا نہ کہ ماں کی جانب سے، چنانچہ اس امر میں یہ آیت اشارة انس ہے
His saying: 'As for istidlal bi-isharat al-nass (inference by indication of the text)' — terminological definition: It is acting upon what is established by its wording in a linguistic sense, but it is not intended nor was the speech brought for it, and it is not apparent from every angle. That is, in terms of language, a meaning is established from the word, and acting upon it in such a manner that it is not intended, nor was the speech brought for it, nor is it apparent from all aspects. Benefits of the restrictions: 'bi-nazmihi' is a genus that includes ishara as well as ibara, because just as isharat al-nass relates to the text, so does ibarat al-nass. Thus there is need for such restrictions that make the definition comprehensive for ishara and exclusive of other things. (1) 'lughatan': this restriction excludes the meaning that is established as iqtida' al-nass (requirement of the text), because that is not based on linguistic implication, but its basis is sometimes reason. (2) 'lakinnahu ghayru maqsudin wa la sabaqa lahu al-nass': this restriction excludes ibarat al-nass, because that is intended and the speech is brought for that purpose. The commentator opines that the author's statement 'laysa bi-zahirin min kulli wajhin' is not a restrictive qualification, but rather gives additional emphasis. In other words, from this the reason for its name 'ishara' is known: it is called ishara because it is not apparent, not the original. Sensory example of ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass: The commentator gave this sensory example: when a person looks at another person with a comprehensive gaze and complete intent and will, then simultaneously with peripheral vision he also looks at the things to his right and left, even though these are not intended. So looking with intent is ibarat al-nass, and the rest is isharat al-nass. Example of isharat al-nass: Allah Almighty says: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing.' The author of Nur al-Anwar says that the lam in 'al-mawlud lahu' is for specification (ikhtisas), from which it is understood that the lineage of children goes to their father, not to the mother. Thus in this matter, this verse is isharat al-nass.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a terminological definition of 'al-istidlal bi-isharat al-nass' (inference by indication of the text). The author first gives the definition: it is acting upon a meaning that is established by the wording in a linguistic sense, but that meaning is not the primary intent of the speaker, nor was the text brought for that purpose, and it is not evident from every angle. This distinguishes it from ibarat al-nass (explicit meaning), where the meaning is intended and the text is brought for it. The commentator then explains the purpose of each restriction in the definition. The word 'bi-nazmihi' is a genus that includes both ishara and ibara, so other restrictions are needed to exclude ibara. The restriction 'lughatan' excludes iqtida' al-nass, which relies on reason rather than language. The restriction 'ghayru maqsud' excludes ibara. The phrase 'laysa bi-zahirin min kulli wajhin' is not a separate condition but emphasizes that ishara is not as apparent as ibara, hence its name. The commentator provides a sensory example: when you look at a person with full intent, you also peripherally notice things around them; the intentional gaze is ibara, the peripheral is ishara. Then a Shariah example: the Qur'anic verse 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing' (2:233) uses the lam of specification, implying that the child's lineage is from the father, not the mother. This ruling is derived by ishara, as it is not the primary meaning but is linguistically implied.

Key Terms
اشارة النص (isharat al-nass): A meaning established by the wording linguistically, but not intended nor the speech brought for it, and not apparent from every angle.
عبارة النص (ibarat al-nass): The explicit meaning that is intended by the speaker and for which the text was brought.
نص (nass): A clear definitive text (Quran or Hadith) that is evident in meaning.
اقتضاء النص (iqtida' al-nass): A meaning that is not linguistically expressed but is rationally necessary for the validity of the explicit ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass?
A) Ibarat al-nass is based on reason, isharat al-nass on language.
B) Ibarat al-nass is the intended meaning, isharat al-nass is not the primary intent.
C) Ibarat al-nass is always apparent, isharat al-nass is hidden.
D) Ibarat al-nass applies to Quran only, isharat al-nass to Hadith only.

Key Takeaway
Isharat al-nass is a binding linguistic implication of a text, distinct from explicit meaning (ibara) and rational necessity (iqtida'), and its conditions ensure it is not mistakenly elevated to primary intent.

Conflict Between Ibarat al-Nass and Isharat al-Nass
States the rule for resolving conflict between ibara and ishara from the same text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of precedence when ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass conflict from the same textual source.

Core Idea
When a single text yields conflicting rulings, the explicit meaning (ibara) overrides the implied (ishara).

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental rule of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: how to resolve a conflict between the explicit and implied meanings of the same text. Both ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass are authoritative, but when they collide, the direct indication prevails. The matn states this clearly, and the commentary illustrates it with a hadith example.

Guided Path
1
Define ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass
Recall the definitions from previous lessons. Ibarat al-nass is the explicit, intended meaning; isharat al-nass is the implied, unintended meaning.
2
Understand their shared authority
Both are qat'i (definitive) in indicating their own rulings. The matn says 'both are equal in obligating the ruling'.
3
Identify the conflict scenario
When one text yields two different rulings: one from ibara and another from ishara.
4
Apply the rule of precedence
Ibarat al-nass takes priority because it is 'awla wa adall' (more primary and more indicative) of the text's intent.
5
Analyze the given example
The hadith about women's deficiency: the explicit statement is the ruling; any implied ruling must defer to it.
The example is incomplete in the text but the principle is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وهما سواء فى ايجاب الحكم الا ان لاول احق عنه التعارض هذه عبارت سے ماتن عبارة النص اور اشارۃ النص سے ثابت ہونے والے احکام کا مشترک اثر (حکم) بیان فرمارہے ہیں کہ یہ دونوں اپنی مراد پر دلالت کرنے میں قطعی ہیں۔ وجه فرق ان دونوں میں فرق تعارض کے وقت ہو گا کہ جب ایک ہی نص سے بطور عبارۃ انس ایک حکم اور بطور اشارة النص دوسرا حکم معلوم ہورہا ہے تو ترجیح اس حکم کو ہوگی جو عبارة النص سے ثابت ہو کیونکہ عبارة النص اشارہ النص سے اولی و ادل على النص ہے شاریخ نے اس کی مثال بیان کی ہے کہ نبی کریم اے نے عورتوں کے متعلق فرمایا کہ وہ دین و عقل دونوں اعتبار سے مردوں کے مقابلے میں ناقص ہیں ۔ جب صحابیات نے پوچھا کہ ہم میں کیا کی
His saying: 'And both are equal in obligating the ruling, except that the first (ibara) has more right in case of conflict.' This statement of the matn (author) expresses the common effect (ruling) of the rulings established by ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass — that both are definitive (qat'i) in indicating their meaning. The aspect of difference: The difference between them occurs at the time of conflict: when from a single text, one ruling is understood by way of ibarat al-nass and another ruling by way of isharat al-nass, then preference is given to the ruling established by ibarat al-nass, because ibarat al-nass is more primary and more indicative of the text than isharat al-nass. The commentator gave an example of this: that the Prophet ﷺ said concerning women: 'They are deficient in religion and intellect compared to men.' When the female companions asked: 'What is (the deficiency) in us?'
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage explains a rule from the matn: both ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass are equally definitive (qat'i) in establishing their respective rulings as long as they do not conflict. However, if they do conflict — meaning from the same text, one ruling is derived explicitly (ibara) and another ruling is derived implicitly (ishara) — then precedence is given to the ruling from ibarat al-nass. The reason is that ibara is the primary method of indication (dalala) and is more directly linked to the text's intent. The commentator provides a hadith example: The Prophet ﷺ said that women are deficient in religion and intellect. The explicit (ibara) meaning is the statement itself about deficiency. The implied (ishara) meaning might be that women are not fully accountable or something else, but the example is cut off. Nonetheless, the rule is clear: when a single text yields two possible rulings, one via ibara and another via ishara, the ibara ruling takes priority.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict between two proofs that indicate conflicting rulings.
عبارة النص (ibarat al-nass): The explicit, intended meaning of a text.
اشارة النص (isharat al-nass): The implied, unintended linguistic meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a single text yields conflicting rulings by ibarat al-nass and isharat al-nass, which ruling is given preference?
A) The ruling from isharat al-nass, because it is more subtle.
B) The ruling from ibarat al-nass, because it is more primary and indicative.
C) Both are equally valid and a third source must be consulted.
D) The ruling that is more beneficial to the community.

Key Takeaway
Ibarat al-nass takes precedence over isharat al-nass when both derive from the same text and conflict, because ibara is more directly indicative of the text's primary intent.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Dalalat al-Nass: Definition and Absence of 'Umum
Defines dalalat al-nass and its properties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define dalalat al-nass, distinguish it from qiyas, and explain why rulings established by it lack general applicability (umum).

Core Idea
Dalalat al-nass extends a ruling via necessary implication — but that ruling is not general.

In this lesson, we explore a distinctive Hanafi proof method: dalalat al-nass. Unlike explicit wording or analogy, this method derives rulings that are necessarily implied by the text. We will see how the Hanafi school uses it to extend a ruling beyond the literal words, and why such rulings are not subject to specification (takhsis) due to the absence of 'umum.

Guided Path
1
Define dalalat al-nass
Identify the definition: a meaning immediately understood from the wording without being hidden, requiring no external proof.
The source defines it as 'ma huwa ma'lum min mujarrad al-lafz li kull ahl al-lugha wa ghayr makhfi'.
2
Identify the inter-school dispute
Contrast the Hanafi acceptance with the Shafi'i rejection; note the differing examples concerning kaffarah in Ramadan.
Imam al-Shafi'i considers such extension to be qiyas, not direct implication.
3
Explain the absence of 'umum
Understand that 'umum is an attribute of words, but dalalat al-nass attaches to meanings necessary from the text. Also, being based on a cause ('illa), it lacks capacity for specification.
The commentator stresses: 'al-umum wa al-khusus min 'awarid al-lafz la al-ma'na'.
4
Apply to the Quranic example
Analyze the verse 'do not say 'uff' (17:23). By dalalat al-nass, hitting parents is also prohibited because it causes greater harm — the same 'illa is present.
This illustration shows how the ruling extends without being general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں عمداً روزے کا فاسد کرنا ہے، لہذا یہ علت جسمیں بھی پائی جانے والی کفارہ لازم کر دیائے گا۔ بلکہ اسی واقعے میں اعرابی کی بیوئی پر کفارہ بھی اسی قبیل سے ہے۔ اگر کوئی شخص نہار رمضان میں عمداً جماع نہ کرے بلکہ کھا پی لے تو اس پر بھی یہی حکم لاگو ہوگا۔
امام شافعی کا اختلاف:
امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ وجوب کفارہ کو صرف اسی شخص کے ساتھہ خاص کرتے ہیں جس نے عمد انبار رمضان میں جماع کیا ہو۔ لہذا ان کے نزدیک عمداً کھا پی کر روزہ فاسد کرنے والے پر کفارہ نہیں
دلیل:
وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نص سے اس کفارہ کی جماع کے ساتھ خصوصیت معلوم ہوتی ہے لہذا حکم جماع میں محصوررہیگا۔ اور اس کے علاوہ فساد صوم عمداً کی دوسری صورتوں کو شامل نہیں ہوگا۔ نکتہ: ۔۔۔۔۔۔ دلالتہ النص کی تعریف یہ کی گئی ہے کہ جو محض لفظ سنگر ہر ما ہر لغت کو معلوم ہو جا نے اور مخفی نہ ہو ۔ حضرت امام شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کے دلالت النص کا انکار کرنے کی بناء پر علمائے اصول نے کہا ہے کہ ان مثال هذه الاحكام فى الدلالة لا يحسن - شارخ کا بھی میں خیال ہے کہ اس طرح کی مثالوں کا اثبات قیاس سے کرنا چاہئے ۔
قوله : والثابت به لا يحتمل التخصيص لانه لا عموم له الخ اس عبارت سے صاحب کتاب رحمہ اللہ ولالہ انس سے ثابت ہونے والے احکام کے متعلق تخصیص کی نفی کو بیان فرمارتے ہیں کہ ایسے احکام میں تخصیص کا احتمال نہیں ہوتا۔ عدم احتمال تخصیص کی وجہ : ۔۔۔۔۔ جس چیز کے اندر حموم ہوتا ہے اس میں تخصیص کو قبول کرنے کی صلاحیت ہوتی ہے۔ جبکہ دلالتہ ان میں عموم ہی نہیں ہوتا ۔ لہذا اسمیں تخصیص کا احتمال کو نہیں پایا جاتا۔
دلالۃ النص میں عموم کیوں نہیں ہوتا:
شارح علام رحمہ اللہ اس امر کی تشریح فرماتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ عموم اور خصوص کا تعلق الفاظ کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اور دلالۃ النص سے ثابت ہونے والے احکام معنی موضوع کو لازم ہوتے ہیں نہ کہ الفاظ کو، لہذا ان میں عموم نہیں، پایا جاتا۔ لانه من عوارض اللفظ لا المعنى
دوسری وجہ : شارح رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے عدم عموم کی دوسری وجہ یہ بیان فرمائی ہے کہ دالتہ النص کا مدار علت پر ہے اور آمیں غیر عات کا احتمال نہیں ہو سکتا لہذا اسمیں تخصیص کا احتمال بھی نہیں ہوگا۔
مثال سے وضاحت:
اللہ تعالی نے والدین کے متعلق اولاد کو حکم فرمایا ہے، فلا تقل لهما اف ولا تنهرهما اور دلالة النص سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ والدین کو مارنا گالی گلوچ کرنا حرام ہے، کیونکہ اسمیں از بیت کا اعلیٰ درجہ پایا جانا ہے جو تا فیف اور مہر بسنے کی حرمت کی علت ہے ۔ اب جہاں علت ) والدین کی اذیت رسانی ) پائی جائے گی وہاں حراست ضرور ہوگی ۔ ورنہ علت اور معلول میں تخالف لازم آئیگا۔ جو بیان نہیں ۔ شارح رحمۃ اللہ علیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس از دم کو عموم اسلئے نہیں کہا جا سکتا کہ عموم خواری الفاظ سے ہے اور یہاں عموم پر دلالت کرنے والا کوئی لفظ نہیں پایا جاتا۔
It is to intentionally invalidate the fast, so wherever this cause is found, it will necessitate expiation. Rather, in that same incident of the Bedouin, the expiation upon his wife is also of this category. If a person in Ramadan intentionally does not have intercourse but eats or drinks, then the same ruling will apply to him.
The disagreement of Imam al-Shafi'i:
Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) restricts the obligation of expiation only to the person who intentionally had intercourse in Ramadan. Therefore, according to him, there is no expiation upon the one who intentionally invalidates the fast by eating or drinking.
Evidence:
He says that from the text the particularization of this expiation with intercourse is known, so the ruling remains confined to intercourse. And it will not include other forms of intentional invalidation of fasting. Point: ... The definition of dalalat al-nass is that which is known from the mere wording to every person of language and is not hidden. Due to Imam al-Shafi'i's denial of dalalat al-nass, the scholars of usul have said that such examples of rulings in indication are not good - the commentator also thinks that the proof of such examples should be through qiyas.
His statement: 'And what is established by it is not subject to specification because it has no generality...' With this phrase, the author (may Allah have mercy on him) expresses the negation of specification regarding rulings established through [dalalat al-nass], that such rulings have no probability of specification. The reason for the absence of probability of specification: ... A thing that has generality has the capacity to accept specification. While dalalat al-nass does not have generality at all. Therefore, it does not have the probability of specification.
Why is there no generality in dalalat al-nass?
The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) explains this matter saying that generality and particularity are related to words, and the rulings established through dalalat al-nass are necessary for the intended meaning, not for the words, therefore they do not have generality. Because it [generality] is an attribute of the word, not the meaning.
Second reason: The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) stated the second reason for the absence of generality: that dalalat al-nass is based on the 'illa (cause), and 'illa cannot accept probability of other things, therefore it will not have probability of specification.
Clarification with example:
Allah ta'ala commanded children regarding parents: 'So do not say to them 'uff' nor reprimand them' [Quran 17:23]. And from dalalat al-nass it is established that hitting and abusing parents is prohibited, because in it [the saying 'uff'] the highest degree of annoyance is found, which is the 'illa for the prohibition of disrespect and harshness. Now wherever the 'illa (causing harm to parents) is found, there prohibition will necessarily occur. Otherwise, contradiction between 'illa and ma'lul would arise, which is not permissible. The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) says that this [ruling] cannot be called general because generality is from the attributes of words, and here there is no word that indicates generality.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on dalalat al-nass, its definition, and its characteristics. It begins by presenting a fiqh example: if someone intentionally breaks the fast by eating or drinking, is expiation (kaffarah) obligatory? The Hanafi position, based on dalalat al-nass, says yes, because the cause (intentional invalidation) is the same as in the case of intercourse. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that kaffarah is specific to intercourse based on the text. This illustrates that dalalat al-nass is a method of extending a ruling via the underlying cause. The author then defines dalalat al-nass as a meaning that is clearly understood from the wording without being hidden. Due to the Shafi'i rejection of this method, scholars of usul mention that such examples are actually based on qiyas. Next, the passage explains that what is established by dalalat al-nass cannot be subject to specification (takhsis) because it lacks generality ('umum). Generality is an attribute of words, but dalalat al-nass deals with meanings that are necessary to the text, not the words themselves. Also, because it relies on the 'illa (cause), and causes do not have generality, specification is impossible. The example of the Quranic verse 'Do not say to them 'uff' ' is used: by dalalat al-nass, hitting parents is also prohibited because it is a greater harm. This ruling is not general but is tied to the presence of the cause.

Key Terms
دلالۃ النص (dalālatu al-naṣṣ): A meaning that is immediately understood from the wording without being hidden, requiring no additional proof.
عموم (ʿumūm): Generality that applies to all individuals of a category; it is an attribute of words.
علت (ʿillah): The effective cause that connects the ruling to its underlying rationale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, why does a person who intentionally eats in Ramadan also incur kaffarah?
A) Because the text explicitly mentions eating.
B) Because the ruling is taken from qiyas on intercourse.
C) Because dalalat al-nass shows that the cause (intentional invalidation) is common.
D) Because of general consensus.

Key Takeaway
Dalalat al-nass derives rulings from necessary textual implication; these rulings are binding but lack generality because 'umum is a property of words, not meanings.

Iqtida' al-Nass: Definition and Prerequisite
Introduces iqtida' al-nass as a usul concept where the text requires a prerequisite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define iqtida' al-nass and identify its prerequisite condition in a usul al-fiqh context.

Core Idea
Iqtida' al-nass: the text's ruling requires an unstated condition to be operative.

In the study of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding iqtida' al-nass is essential for grasping how texts imply necessary conditions. This concept helps us derive rulings from the Quran and Sunnah when the text itself does not explicitly mention a prerequisite. This lesson defines iqtida' al-nass and highlights its core prerequisite.

Guided Path
1
Understand the lexical meaning
Iqtida' al-nass literally means 'the requirement of the text.' In Arabic, iqtida' is the verbal noun meaning 'to demand' or 'to necessitate.'
2
Grasp the technical definition
Technically, iqtida' al-nass refers to a text that does not function except with an unstated condition. The ruling of the text is dependent on that condition.
3
Identify the prerequisite
The passage states: 'The text does not function except with a condition precedent.' That condition must be necessary for the text's ruling to be applicable.
4
Distinguish from dalalat al-nass
Iqtida' al-nass is often confused with dalalat al-nass (implied meaning). In iqtida', the text requires a condition; in dalalat, the text implies an additional ruling. This distinction is important for correct istinbat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله اما الثابت باقتضاء النص فما لا يعمل النص الا بشرط (۴) استدلال باقتضاء النص تقدمه الخ.
لغوی معنی: چیز کا نہ تقاضہ کرے اس مقتضائے نص سے دلیل پکڑنا ۔
الطلاق تعريف: - لا تعمل النص الا بشرط تقدمه
His statement: 'As for what is established by iqtida' al-nass, it is that the text only functions with a condition precedent.' (4) Istidlal bi-iqtida' al-nass... Lexical meaning: Taking evidence from the requirement of the text that a thing necessitates. Definition: The text does not function except with a condition precedent.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This brief passage introduces iqtida' al-nass (required implication of the text). It defines it as a situation where a text's ruling is only operative if a certain condition or prerequisite is assumed. For example, when the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'The divorcer is the husband,' it implies that the divorce is effective only if the husband is sane and adult. The text's ruling depends on that unstated condition. This is a form of dalil that is weaker than explicit text but still binding. The lexical meaning is 'to take evidence from the requirement of the text.' The author states that the text does not function except with a prior condition.

Key Terms
اقتضاء النص (iqtiḍāʾu al-naṣṣ): A text's requirement of an unstated condition for its ruling to be applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the definition of iqtida' al-nass?
A) The text clearly states all conditions.
B) The text functions only if a condition is met, even if not mentioned.
C) The text can be abrogated.
D) The text applies generally to all situations.

Key Takeaway
Iqtida' al-nass is a Hanafi usul concept where a text's ruling is contingent upon an unstated condition that is necessary for its application.

Why Dalalat al-Nass Lacks Generality in Hanafi Usul
Explains two reasons why dalalat al-nass lacks generality in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish rulings derived from explicit wording (nass) from those derived from the underlying cause (dalalat al-nass) and explain why the latter does not carry generality in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Dalalat al-nass lacks generality because it is based on the underlying cause, not on words; generality is a property of words.

In Hanafi usul, rulings can be derived not only from the explicit wording of a text but also from the meaning or cause implied by that wording. This passage addresses a crucial limitation: such rulings do not have generality (umum). The commentator gives two clear reasons that help us understand the boundaries of textual inference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal concept: umum vs. dalalat al-nass
Understand that generality (umum) is a property of words—it indicates that a ruling applies to all individuals of a category. Dalalat al-nass, by contrast, is a ruling derived from the underlying meaning or cause of the text, not from the words themselves. This distinction sets the stage for the two reasons.
2
Examine the first reason: Generality belongs to words, not meanings
The commentator states that umum and particularity (khussus) are attributes of words. The rulings established by dalalat al-nass are necessary for the intended meaning (ma'na) that is inherent to the subject, not for the wording. Therefore, generality cannot be found in them.
3
Examine the second reason: Dalalat al-nass rests on the 'illah, which does not admit generality
Dalalat al-nass is based on the 'illah (effective cause). Since an 'illah is a specific attribute that necessitates a specific ruling, it cannot be general; nor can it be subject to specification (takhsihs). The passage states that a general thing cannot be an 'illah for a particular, so the derived ruling is limited to cases where the 'illah is present.
4
Apply the concept to the example: the verse 'فلا تقل لهما اف ولا تنهرهما'
The verse explicitly forbids saying 'uff' and rebuking parents. By dalalat al-nass, any greater harm (hitting, abusing) is also forbidden because the underlying 'illah—causing harm to parents—is found in greater degree. However, this prohibition is not considered general (umum) because no word in the text indicates generality; it is derived from the 'illah alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دلالۃ النص میں عموم کیوں نہیں ہوتا: شارح علام رحمہ اللہ اس امر کی تشریح فرماتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ عموم اور خصوص کا تعلق الفاظ کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اور دلالۃ النص سے ثابت ہونے والے احکام معنی موضوع کو لازم ہوتے ہیں نہ کہ الفاظ کو، لہذا ان میں عموم نہیں، پایا جاتا۔ لانه من عوارض اللفظ لا المعنى دوسری وجہ : شارح رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے عدم عموم کی دوسری وجہ یہ بیان فرمائی ہے کہ دالتہ النص کا مدار علت پر ہے اور آمیں غیر عات کا احتمال نہیں ہو سکتا لہذا اسمیں تخصیص کا احتمال بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ مثال سے وضاحت: اللہ تعالی نے والدین کے متعلق اولاد کو حکم فرمایا ہے، فلا تقل لهما اف ولا تنهرهما اور دلالة النص سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ والدین کو مارنا گالی گلوچ کرنا حرام ہے، کیونکہ اسمیں از بیت کا اعلیٰ درجہ پایا جانا ہے جو تا فیف اور مہر بسنے کی حرمت کی علت ہے ۔ اب جہاں علت ) والدین کی اذیت رسانی ) پائی جائے گی وہاں حراست ضرور ہوگی ۔ ورنہ علت اور معلول میں تخالف لازم آئیگا۔ جو بیان نہیں ۔ شارح رحمۃ اللہ علیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس از دم کو عموم اسلئے نہیں کہا جا سکتا کہ عموم خواری الفاظ سے ہے اور یہاں عموم پر دلالت کرنے والا کوئی لفظ نہیں پایا جاتا۔
Why dalalat al-nass does not have generality: The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) explains this matter, saying that generality and particularity are related to words, and the rulings established by dalalat al-nass are necessary for the intended meaning, not for words; therefore, generality is not found in them. Because it is an attribute of the word, not the meaning. The second reason: The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) stated the second reason for the lack of generality: that dalalat al-nass is based on the 'illah (cause), and the general cannot be [illah] for the particular? so there is no possibility of specification (takhsis) in it. Clarification by example: Allah Most High commanded children regarding parents: 'Do not say to them 'uff' and do not rebuke them.' From dalalat al-nass it is established that hitting parents, abusing, and cursing them is haram, because in it the highest degree of harm is found, which is the 'illah for the prohibition of oppression and hitting? Now wherever the 'illah (causing harm to parents) is found, there the prohibition is necessarily established. Otherwise, an inconsistency between 'illah and ma'lool would be necessary, which is invalid. The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) says that this prohibition cannot be called general (umum) because generality is from the properties of words, and here there is no word indicating generality.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (usul rule) explaining why dalalat al-nass (indication of the text through meaning, not explicit wording) does not carry generality (umum). The commentator gives two reasons. First, generality and particularity are attributes of words, but dalalat al-nass derives from the underlying meaning (ma'na) that is inherent to the subject matter, not from the wording itself. Second, dalalat al-nass operates on the basis of an 'illah (effective cause), and an 'illah does not admit of generality because it is a specific attribute that necessitates a specific ruling. The example given is the Quranic verse prohibiting saying 'uff' to parents. Through dalalat al-nass, it is deduced that hitting or abusing parents is also haram because it involves a higher degree of harm. This specific prohibition, however, is not considered general (umum) because no word indicates generality; rather, it is derived from the 'illah. This analysis is typical of Hanafi usul, distinguishing between textual generality (umum lafzi) and the scope of rulings derived via 'illah.

Key Terms
دلالۃ النص (dalalat al-nass): Indication of the text through meaning, not explicit wording; a ruling derived from the understood cause ('illah) of a textual command.
عموم (umum): Generality; a property of words that encompasses all individuals of a category.
علت (illah): The effective cause that necessitates a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why does the ruling forbidding harm to parents derived from the verse 'فلا تقل لهما اف' not carry generality (umum)?
A) Because the verse is abrogated.
B) Because the ruling is based on the 'illah (cause) of harm, not on a general word.
C) Because the verse only applies to children, not to others.
D) Because the ruling is derived by qiyas, not by literal text.

Key Takeaway
Dalalat al-nass lacks generality because it is based on the 'illah (cause) and not on a general word; generality is a property of words, not meanings.

Preference Between Dhalalat al-Nass and Iqtida' al-Nass
Expanding the principle of iqtida' al-nass and its hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi rule that dhalalat al-nass takes precedence over iqtida' al-nass in case of conflict, and explain why iqtida' al-nass does not carry generality (umum).

Core Idea
Dhalalat al-nass is stronger than iqtida'; in conflict, dhalalat prevails and iqtida' has no generality.

This lesson expands on two key aspects of iqtida' al-nass (textual implication): how it is distinguished from dhalalat al-nass (textual indication), and the Hanafi position regarding its generality. Through a Quranic example and a hadith example, you will learn the mechanism of iqtida' and the rule of preference when these two types of indication conflict. The passage also highlights an important ikhtilaf with other schools: whether a ruling established by iqtida' carries generality.

Guided Path
1
Define iqtida' al-nass with an example
Identify the Quranic command 'fa tahriru raqabah' (free a slave). Notice that the word 'raqabah' is general, but it is rationally and legally impossible to free another's slave for expiation. Therefore, the text necessarily implies the restriction 'owned slave' (mamlukah). This implication is iqtida' al-nass.
Iqtida' is a necessary implication for the text to be valid.
2
Apply the preference rule
Read the rule: when a ruling from dhalalat al-nass conflicts with one from iqtida' al-nass, dhalalat is preferred because it is stronger (aqwa). Note the example: the hadith about washing impurity with water (iqtida' implies water is required) vs. dhalalat from other texts that any pure liquid works. The dhalalat prevails.
Dhalalat includes meanings derived from context, priority, or equal applicability.
3
Analyze the hadith example for iqtida'
The Prophet told 'A'ishah to scratch, rub, and wash impurity with water. By iqtida', water is the only means of purification (otherwise impurity remains). But dhalalat shows that other pure liquids also purify. The preference is given to dhalalat, so purification is not limited to water.
This shows that iqtida' is weaker and does not override dhalalat.
4
Examine the dispute over generality
The author states 'there is no generality in iqtida' according to us' (la 'umum lahu 'indana). This is a disputed issue: other schools may hold that iqtida' retains generality. The Hanafi position is that iqtida' is a limited implication, specific to the necessary context, not extendable.
This ikhtilaf has practical implications for analogical reasoning (qiyas).
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
Recap: (1) Iqtida' al-nass is a valid but weaker form of indication. (2) In conflict, dhalalat prevails. (3) Iqtida' does not produce a general ruling; it is confined to the specific necessity.
This hierarchy ensures systematic reliance on stronger textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والثابت منه كا لثابت بدلالة النص الا عنه المعارضه الخ تشریح عبارت : ۔۔۔ اس عبارت سے دور فائدے حاصل ہو رہے ہیں:۔ (1) الثابت بالا قتضاء النص ( مقتضی ) کی مثال (۲) تعارض کے وقت دلالۃ النص کی وجہ ترجیح۔ ہم ترتیب وار اختصار سے دونوں باتیں بیان کریں گے۔ (1) الثابت بالاقتضاء النص کی مثال : --- قال الله تبارك و تعالى في الكفارات : فتحرير رقبة لفظ کے عموم کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ رقبہ کا لفظ رقبہ معلوم کہ اور غیر مملوکہ سب کو شامل ہو لیکن یہ بات شرعاً اور عقلا نا جائز ہے کہ غیر کے غلام کے ذریعہ کفارہ ادا ہو جائے۔ لہذا اقتضاء النص کے طریق پر رقبہ کے ساتھ مملوکہ کی قید مانا ضروری ہے۔ (۲) تعارض کے وقت دلالۃ النص کی وجہ ترجیح: جس طرح دلالۃ النص ایجاب حکم میں مفید ہے اسی طرح اقتضاء النص بھی ہے۔ لیکن اگر ایک حکم دلالۃ النص سے ثابت ہو اور اسکے برعکس حکم اقتضاء النص سے ثابت ہو یعنی دونوں کا باہم تعارض ہو جائے تو اس حکم کو ترجیح دی جائے گی جو دلالۃ النص سے ثابت ہو، کیونکہ یہ اقوئی ہے۔ والا قومی راجح عند التعارض . مثال سے قاعدہ مذکورہ کی وضاحت: ناپاک کپڑوں کی طہارت کے متعلق سرکار دو عالم میں اللہ نے اماں عائشہ صدیقہ ام المؤمنین رضی اللہ عنھا سے فرمایا تھا: حتيه ثم اقرصيه ثم اغسليه بالماء (پہلے رگڑو پھر کھرچ دو، پھر پانی سے دھوڈالو ) اس حدیث سے بطریق اقتضاء النص یہ بات معلوم ہوئی کہ طہارت کے لئے غسل بالماء شرط ہے ورنہ نا پاک چیز پاک نہیں ہوگی۔ لیکن دلالة النص سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ پانی کی طرح دوسرے مائعات (سیال یعنی بہنے والی پاک چنہیں ) بھی پاکی کے لئے مفید ہیں۔ تعارض کا حل یہ ہے کہ پاکی پانی کے ساتھ خاص نہیں بلکہ ہر طاہر سیال شئے اس کے لئے مفید ہے هذا ترجيح حكم الدلالة على الاقتضاء لان الدلالة اقوى . قوله : ولا عموم له عندنا لان العموم والخصوص الخ حل عبارت: - صاحب کتاب رحمہ اللہ یہاں سے یہ بات بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ جو حکم اقتضاء کے طریقے پر ثابت ہوا اس میں عموم نہیں۔ یہ ایک اختلافی مسئلہ ہے: (1) احناف کا مذھب: اقتضاء النص کے قسم [محصن؟] میں نہیں۔ احناف مقتضی میں عدم عموم کے قائل ہیں۔
His saying: 'And what is established by it is like what is established by the indication of the text, except when there is contradiction...' Explanation of the phrase: Two benefits are obtained from this phrase: (1) an example of what is established by iqtida' al-nass (muqtada), (2) the preference of dhalalat al-nass in case of conflict. We will explain both in order. (1) Example of what is established by iqtida' al-nass: Allah Most High said concerning expiations: '...freeing a slave (raqabah).' The generality of the word requires that 'raqabah' includes both known (owned) and unowned (unowned) slaves, but it is legally and rationally impermissible that a slave of another should serve as expiation. Therefore, by way of iqtida' al-nass, it is necessary to assume the restriction of ownership (mamlukah) with 'raqabah.' (2) The preference of dhalalat al-nass in case of conflict: Just as dhalalat al-nass is useful for establishing a ruling, so too iqtida' al-nass. But if one ruling is established by dhalalat al-nass and the opposite ruling by iqtida' al-nass, i.e., they contradict, then preference is given to the ruling established by dhalalat al-nass, because it is stronger. And the preferred is the stronger in case of conflict. Clarification of the mentioned principle with an example: Concerning the purification of impure clothes, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her): 'Scratch it, then rub it, then wash it with water.' From this hadith, by way of iqtida' al-nass, it is understood that washing with water is a condition for purification; otherwise the impure thing would not become pure. But from dhalalat al-nass it is understood that other liquids (pure flowing things) are also useful for purification, like water. The resolution of the contradiction is that purification is not specific to water, but every pure liquid is useful for it. This is the preference of the ruling of dhalalat over iqtida' because dhalalat is stronger. His saying: 'And there is no generality in it according to us, because generality and specificity...' Explanation: The author (may Allah have mercy on him) is stating here that the ruling established by way of iqtida' has no generality. This is a disputed issue. (1) The madhhab of the Hanafis: [There is no generality] in the category of iqtida' al-nass. The Hanafis hold absence of generality in muqtada.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the principle of iqtida' al-nass (textual implication) and its relationship with dhalalat al-nass (textual indication). The author first gives an example of iqtida' al-nass: the Quranic command to free a slave (raqabah) in expiation. The general word 'raqabah' would include both owned and unowned slaves, but since freeing an unowned slave is impossible, the text necessarily implies the restriction 'owned' (mamlukah). This is iqtida' al-nass. Then the author establishes a rule: when a ruling from dhalalat al-nass conflicts with one from iqtida' al-nass, dhalalat is preferred because it is stronger. The example given is the hadith instructing the washing of impurity with water. Iqtida' al-nass implies water is essential, but dhalalat al-nass from other texts shows that any pure liquid suffices. Therefore, the ruling from dhalalat takes precedence. Finally, the author notes that according to the Hanafis, rulings established by iqtida' al-nass do not have generality (umum). This is a point of ikhtilaf with other schools. The passage illustrates how Hanafi usul prioritizes textual indications systematically.

Key Terms
اقتضاء النص (iqtida' al-nass): A ruling established by necessary implication of the text, without which the text would be legally or rationally impossible.
دلالۃ النص (dhalalat al-nass): A ruling derived from the text's explicit or contextual indication, such as meaning by priority or equal applicability.
عموم (umum): Generality of a ruling, applying to all individuals covered by the text's words.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Dhalalat al-nass, because it is stronger in indication.
C) Both are equal; preference is arbitrary.
D) Neither; the conflict remains unresolved.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, dhalalat al-nass is preferred over iqtida' al-nass when they conflict, and rulings established by iqtida' do not carry generality.

Preference of Dalaalat al-Nass over Iqtidaa al-Nass
States the rule for preferring dalaalat al-nass over iqtidaa al-nass

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between dalaalat al-nass and iqtidaa al-nass and apply the rule that dalaalat al-nass is preferred when they conflict.

Core Idea
Dalaalat al-nass is stronger than iqtidaa al-nass; it prevails when they conflict.

In Hanafi usul, two types of textual inference exist: explicit implication (dalaalat al-nass) and implied necessity (iqtidaa al-nass). This passage explains why and how the stronger inference takes precedence. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for deriving rulings from texts correctly.

Guided Path
1
Define the two modes of textual implication
Dalaalat al-nass is the explicit meaning without needing to assume an omitted element. Iqtidaa al-nass requires assuming an omission to make sense of the statement.
2
State the preference rule
When a ruling from dalaalat al-nass conflicts with one from iqtidaa al-nass, the former is given precedence because it is stronger.
3
Examine the example from the hadith
The Prophet ﷺ instructed to wash an impurity with water. Iqtidaa implies washing is a condition for purification. Dalaalat indicates water is an example, not exclusive.
4
Resolve the conflict
Since dalaalat is stronger, we conclude that any pure liquid suffices for purification.
This is a Hanafi position; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) تعارض کے وقت دلالۃ النص کی وجہ ترجیح: جس طرح دلالۃ النص ایجاب حکم میں مفید ہے اسی طرح اقتضاء النص بھی ہے۔ لیکن اگر ایک حکم دلالۃ النص سے ثابت ہو اور اسکے برعکس حکم اقتضاء النص سے ثابت ہو یعنی دونوں کا باہم تعارض ہو جائے تو اس حکم کو ترجیح دی جائے گی جو دلالۃ النص سے ثابت ہو، کیونکہ یہ اقوئی ہے۔ والا قومی راجح عند التعارض . مثال سے قاعدہ مذکورہ کی وضاحت: ناپاک کپڑوں کی طہارت کے متعلق سرکار دو عالم میں اللہ نے اماں عائشہ صدیقہ ام المؤمنین رضی اللہ عنھا سے فرمایا تھا: حتيه ثم اقرصيه ثم اغسليه بالماء (پہلے رگڑو پھر کھرچ دو، پھر پانی سے دھوڈالو ) اس حدیث سے بطریق اقتضاء النص یہ بات معلوم ہوئی کہ طہارت کے لئے غسل بالماء شرط ہے ورنہ نا پاک چیز پاک نہیں ہوگی۔ لیکن دلالة النص سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ پانی کی طرح دوسرے مائعات (سیال یعنی بہنے والی پاک چیزیں ) بھی پاکی کے لئے مفید ہیں۔ تعارض کا حل یہ ہے کہ پاکی پانی کے ساتھ خاص نہیں بلکہ ہر طاہر سیال شئے اس کے لئے مفید ہے هذا ترجيح حكم الدلالة على الاقتضاء لان الدلالة اقوى .
(2) The reason for preferring dalaalat al-nass at the time of conflict: Just as dalaalat al-nass is useful in establishing a ruling, so too is iqtidaa al-nass. But if one ruling is established by dalaalat al-nass and the opposite ruling is established by iqtidaa al-nass, i.e., the two conflict, then preference is given to the ruling established by dalaalat al-nass, because it is stronger. And the stronger is preferred when there is conflict. Clarification of the mentioned rule with an example: Regarding the purification of impure clothes, the leader of both worlds (peace be upon him) said to Lady Aisha Siddiqa, Mother of the Believers (may Allah be pleased with her): 'Rub it, then scratch it, then wash it with water.' From this hadith, by way of iqtidaa al-nass, it is understood that washing with water is a condition for purification, otherwise the impure thing will not become pure. But from dalaalat al-nass it is known that other liquids (i.e., flowing pure liquids) are also useful for purification like water. The resolution of the conflict is that purification is not specific to water, but every pure liquid is useful for it. This is a preference of the ruling of dalaalat over iqtidaa because dalaalat is stronger.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage explains a key usul rule: When two textual implications conflict—one from direct explicit meaning (dalaalat al-nass) and one from implied meaning (iqtidaa al-nass)—the ruling from the explicit meaning takes precedence because it is stronger in evidence. The author illustrates with a hadith: The Prophet ﷺ instructed Aisha (ra) to wash an impurity with water. By iqtidaa, one might conclude that only water purifies. But by dalaalat, other pure liquids also purify, as water is just an example. Since dalaalat is stronger, we prefer the ruling that any pure liquid suffices. This rule is specific to Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
دلالۃ النص (dalaalat al-nass): The explicit meaning indicated by the wording of the text without needing to presume an omitted element.
اقتضاء النص (iqtidaa al-nass): An implied meaning that must be understood from the text by assuming an omitted word or phrase to make the statement sensible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Dalaalat al-nass

D) Neither

Key Takeaway
When dalaalat al-nass and iqtidaa al-nass conflict, dalaalat al-nass prevails because it is a stronger implication.

Generality of Muqtada: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presents the Hanafi view on muqtada and the Shafi'i counterargument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions on generality in muqtada and explain the Hanafi reasoning that restricts 'umum to explicit words.

Core Idea
Muqtada is a meaning, not a word; hence it cannot be general according to Hanafi usul.

This lesson dives into a key dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is: whether the implied meaning (muqtada) derived from iqtidaa al-nass carries generality. The Hanafi school restricts generality to explicit words, while Shafi'is treat muqtada as if it were spoken. Understanding this difference is crucial for correct istinbat in many fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Determine precisely what is being disputed: the applicability of 'umum (generality) to the category of muqtada (the implied meaning required by the text).
2
State the Hanafi position and proof
The Hanafis hold that muqtada has no 'umum. Their proof: 'umum and khusus are accidental properties of words (alfaz), while muqtada is a meaning (ma'na), not a word.
3
State the Shafi'i position and proof
The Shafi'is counter that muqtada does carry 'umum. They consider muqtada like a deleted word (mahdhoof) which is treated as if uttered, so it belongs to the category of words and can be general.
4
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of this difference using a concrete fiqh example: the phrase 'a'tiq 'abdi 'anni' (free my slave on my behalf). Hanafis say the implied sale is not general; Shafi'is say it applies to all slaves.
Different rulings on the number of slaves affected.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text sides with the Hanafi position, as indicated by the opening statement 'Nor is there generality in it according to us.' This is the relied-upon view in Hanafi usul.
The Hanafi view is adopted in the matn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا عموم له عندنا لان العموم والخصوص الخ حل عبارت: - صاحب کتاب رحمہ اللہ یہاں سے یہ بات بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ جو حکم اقتضاء اس کے طریقے پر ثابت ہوا میں عموم نہیں : ۔ سیا ایک اختلافی مسئلہ ہے:۔ (1) احناف کا مذھب: اقتناء انس کے قسم (محصن) میں نہیں ۔ احناف متخضی میں عدم عموم کے قائل ہیں ۔ احناف کی دلیل : ۔ ۔ ۔ عموم اور خصوص الفاظ کے عوارض میں سے ہیں جبکہ مقتضی معنی کی قبیل ہے۔ (۲) شوافع کا مذھب ۔ ۔ ۔ شوافع اہل اصول کے ہاں مقتضی میں عموم ہے شوافع کی دلیل :۔۔ شوافع مقتضی کو محذوف کی طرح قرار دیتے ہیں جو ملفوظ ہوتا ہے لہذا مقتضی بھی الفاظ کی قبیل سے ہوگا ۔ اور اسمیں عموم و خصوص جاری ہو نگے ۔
His statement: 'And there is no generality in it according to us because generality and particularity...' Explanation of the phrase: The author (may Allah have mercy on him) states from here that the ruling established by way of iqtidaa has no generality. This is a point of difference: (1) The Hanafi school: There is no generality in the category of muqtada. The Hanafis believe in lack of generality in muqtada. The Hanafi proof: Generality and particularity are among the accidents of words, whereas muqtada is of the category of meaning. (2) The Shafi'i school: According to the Shafi'i usul scholars, there is generality in muqtada. The Shafi'i proof: The Shafi'is consider muqtada like the omitted (mahdhoof) which is spoken, therefore muqtada is also from the category of words, and generality and particularity apply to it.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage outlines a fundamental dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is. The issue is whether the implied meaning derived by iqtidaa (muqtada) can be considered general ('amm). Hanafis argue that 'umum and khusus are properties of explicit words (alfaz), but muqtada is a meaning (ma'na), not a word, so it cannot be general. Shafi'is counter that muqtada is like a deleted word (mahdhoof), which is considered as if uttered, so it falls under the domain of words and thus can be general. This difference has practical implications in many fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
مقتضی (muqtada): The implied meaning or requirement that is understood from a text by way of iqtidaa al-nass.
عموم ('umum): Generality; a word that encompasses all individuals of its category without restriction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because muqtada is a meaning, not a word
B) Because muqtada is always particular
C) Because the Qur'an forbids it
D) Because the Prophet ﷺ said so

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, muqtada (implied meaning) lacks generality because it belongs to the category of meaning, not to explicit words.
