Nass Does Not Cover Non-Mansus Cases: The Hanafi Principle and the Ansar's Argument
Explaining the Hanafi principle that a nass does not extend beyond its explicit scope, with the Ansar's counter-argument using the definite article.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a nass only covers its explicit case and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the Hanafis and the Ansar regarding ghusl for ihtilam.

Core Idea
A text's silence is not negation; extension requires a separate proof.

This passage addresses a fundamental usul dispute: does an explicit text (nass) automatically cover or negate cases it does not mention? The Hanafis argue it does not; the Ansar (Helpers) used the definite article to claim generality. Understanding this principle is crucial for correct legal derivation, as it affects rulings like ghusl after nocturnal emission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Principle
Start by grasping the core claim: a nass only gives a ruling for the case it explicitly mentions. It is silent about other cases. This is illustrated with Zaid's coming and the hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma'.
The principle is that silence is not negation; it is absence of ruling.
2
Examine the Hanafi Proof (Dalil)
The Hanafis use linguistic examples and a second hadith ('idha jawaza al-khitan al-khitan') to show that the original nass does not cover ihtilam, but another nass does. Identify how each proof functions: the linguistic example establishes the rule; the second hadith provides the ruling for ihtilam.
The second hadith is explicit about ghusl when circumcised parts meet, regardless of emission.
3
Analyze the Ansar's Counter-Argument
The Ansar argued using the definite article (lam) on 'al-ma' to claim generality (istighraq). Understand their reasoning: if 'al-ma' means all water, then ghusl is wajib for all emission, but ihtilam without emission would not trigger it because there is no confirmed water.
They used the lam to imply that the text covers all instances of water, but then concluded that ihtilam without emission is not covered.
4
Study the Hanafi Response
The Hanafis rebut by saying the lam is not for istighraq but for 'ahd or haqiqa. Even if it were, ihtilam is included because it involves sexual desire and presumed discharge. The second hadith confirms the obligation regardless of emission.
The Hanafi response shows how multiple proofs work together: the original nass is limited; another nass covers the remaining case.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis say ghusl is wajib for ihtilam (due to the second hadith or inclusion by desire), while the Ansar's logic would make it not wajib unless actual emission is confirmed. Recognize how this affects fatwa.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text

جواب: متاخرین علماء کا فتوئی اس بات پر ہے کہ روایات فقہی میں تو یہ قاعدہ جاری ہوگا لیکن نصوص شرعیہ میں نہیں مثلاً صاحب ہدایہ نے مدیر عظیم کی یہ تعریف کی ہے کہ اس کی ایک جانب کو حرکت دینے سے جانب آخر میں حرکت کا اثر محسوس نہ ہو آگے فرمایا ہے جاز الوضوء من الجانب الأخر (یعنی جس جانب میں نجاست نہیں گری اس جانب سے وضو جائز ہے ) اس سے یہی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ وقوع نجاست والی جانب سے وضو کرنا جائز نہیں۔
قوله لان النص لم تتناوله فكيف الخ.
احناف کی دلیل: جب نص سے صرف انہی حکم معلوم ہو رہا ہے تو کس طرح غیر منصوص کو ثابت کیا جاسکتا ہے کیونکہ اگر نص اثبات کے متعلق ہے تو نفی غیر منصوص ہے اور نفی صرف منصوص حکم کو شامل ہوتی ہے نہ کہ غیر منصوص کو۔
مثال سے وضاحت: شارخ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی کہے: جاء نی زید تو یہ کلام صرف محبت زید پر دلالت کرتا ہے، رہا مرد کا آنا یا نہ آنا، یہ اس کے متعاق ساکت ہے۔ اسی طرح السماء من الماء اخراج منی سے وجوب غسل پر تو نص ہے رہا اکسال سے وجوب یا عدم وجوب غسل، اس کے متعلق یہ ساکت ہے اور اکس سال سے عمل دوسری حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے اذا جاوز الختان الختان فقد وجب الغسل انزل اولم ينزل۔ اس طرح خمس من الفواسق الخ اسکے علاوہ جانوروں کا حکم معلوم نہیں ہوتا۔
قوله : وفائدة التخصيص الخ : اعتراض: ----- جب اسم علم کی صراحت ماعدا کی نفی میں مفید نہیں تو اس کی صراحت کا کیا فائده؟ جواب: اس طرح کی صراحت کا فائدہ یہ ہے کہ اہل اجتہاد و استنباط دوسرے مواقع پر اس صراحت پر غور و تدبر کر کے بذریعہ قیاس حکم لگائیں تا کہ انہیں مجتہد کا اعلیٰ مقام حاصل ہو کیا یہ کم فائدہ ہے! قوله والاستدلال منهم بحرف الاستغراق الخ
انصار نے تخصیص کا قول کیوں اختیار کیا: مصنف رحمہ اللہ قائلین تخصیص کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ انصار صحابہ رضی اللہ عنھم کے قول کی وجہ یہ نہیں تھی جو آپ نے کبھی بلکہ انہوں نے حدیث میں دونوں جگہ الماء پر داخل ہونے والے لام تعریف کے پیش نظریہ قول کیا تھا۔ کیونکہ استغراق کا یہی تقاضا ہے کہ مسل تمام افراد خروج منی سے واجب ہو ۔ جس کا بدلہ یہی مطلب ہے کہ اگر خروج منی کا تحقیق نہ ہو جس طرح اکسال میں ہے تو غسل بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا ۔
ويرد علينا ديننذ فمن این قلتم الخ
اعتراض: جان لیا کہ انصار کا استدلال لام استغراق سے تھا تب بھی تو حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اکسال کی صورت میں غسل واجب نہیں ہوتا ۔ جب ایسا ہے تو احناف اکسال کی صورت میں غسل کا قول کیوں کرتے ہیں! جواب: ہم بھی تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ وجوب غسل کا تعلق خروج ماء کے ساتھ ہے البتہ جن افراد کا تعلق بھی شہوت کے ماتھے ۔ ہے وہ اس میں داخل ہیں مثلا اکسال۔ اعتراض :۔۔۔۔۔ اس طرح تو حیض و نفاس کے بعد واجب ہونے والا نسل خارج ہو جائے گا
Answer: The later scholars' fatwa is that this rule will apply in juristic narrations but not in Shar'i texts. For example, the author of Hidayah defined a large mill as one whose one side can be moved without the other side feeling the motion. Then he said: 'Wudu is permissible from the other side' (i.e., the side where impurity did not fall). This indicates that wudu from the side where impurity fell is not permissible.
His statement: 'Because the text does not address it, so how...'.
Proof of the Hanafis: When only that ruling is known from the text, how can one prove the non-textual? Because if the text is about affirmation, then negation is non-textual, and negation only includes the textual ruling, not the non-textual.
Clarification by example: The commentator says that if someone says 'Zaid came to me', this speech only indicates Zaid's coming; regarding any man's coming or not, it is silent about it. Similarly, 'water from water' is a text about the obligation of ghusl from emission of semen; regarding the obligation or non-obligation of ghusl from nocturnal emission, it is silent about it. And the ruling on nocturnal emission is known from another hadith: 'When the circumcised parts meet, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether he ejaculates or not.' Similarly, 'five are the harmful animals' — the ruling for other animals is not known from this.
His statement: 'And the benefit of specification...'.
Objection: When the explicitness of a proper noun is not beneficial in negating others, what is the benefit of its explicitness?
Answer: The benefit of such explicitness is that the people of ijtihad and deduction will ponder this explicitness on other occasions and derive rulings through analogy, so that they attain the high rank of a mujtahid. Is this not a great benefit?
His statement: 'And the argument of them with the particle of generality...'.
Why the Ansar adopted the view of specification: The author, may Allah have mercy on him, while answering the proponents of specification, says: The reason for the statement of the Ansar (may Allah be pleased with them) was not what you thought; rather, they made their statement based on the definite article (lam) entering 'al-ma' (water) in both places of the hadith. Because the requirement of generality is that ghusl becomes obligatory for all instances of semen emission. The consequence of this is that if the emission of semen is not confirmed, just as in the case of nocturnal emission, then ghusl would also not be obligatory.
'And it is objected to us that from where do you say...'
Objection: It is understood that the Ansar's argument was with the lam of generality; even then, from the hadith it is known that in the case of nocturnal emission, ghusl is not obligatory. When this is so, why do the Hanafis say that ghusl is obligatory in the case of nocturnal emission?
Answer: We also acknowledge that the obligation of ghusl is tied to the emission of water; however, those individuals that are related to the state of sexual desire are included in it, such as nocturnal emission.
Objection: In this way, the bath obligatory after menstruation and postpartum bleeding would be excluded.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute (ikhtilaf) about the scope of legal texts. The author begins by stating the later Hanafi position: the principle that a text does not cover unmentioned cases applies to juristic narrations (riwayat fiqhiyya) but not to primary scriptural texts (nusus shar'iyya). He illustrates with a fiqh example from the Hidayah about wudu near a millstone with impurity on one side. Then he turns to the core proving of the Hanafis: when a text (nass) establishes a specific ruling, it cannot be extended beyond its explicit scope. He gives linguistic evidence: if someone says 'Zaid came', it only speaks about Zaid; it is silent about other men. Similarly, the hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma' [water from water]' makes ghusl obligatory only for the explicit case of seminal emission; it says nothing about nocturnal emission (ihtilam). The ruling for ihtilam is provided by another hadith: 'When the circumcised parts meet, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether he ejaculates or not.' Likewise, the hadith 'Five are the harmful animals' does not give rulings about other animals. The author then addresses an objection: if explicit mention of a proper noun does not negate others, what is the benefit of such explicitness? The answer: it serves as a basis for qiyas (analogy) by mujtahids. Finally, the author discusses why the Ansar (Helpers) argued for specification (takhsis) using the definite article (lam al-ta'rif) on 'al-ma' (the water) in the hadith. The Ansar claimed it implied generality (istighraq), making ghusl obligatory for all instances of water, so for ihtilam without emission, it would not be obligatory. The Hanafi response: even if one accepts the lam of generality, the ruling is still tied to the actual discharge of water; cases of ihtilam are included because they involve sexual desire and presumed discharge. An objection is raised that this would exclude ghusl after hayd and nifas, but the passage ends without completing the answer.

Key Terms
نص (nass): A clear textual ruling that explicitly states a legal rule for a specific case.
تخصیص (takhsis): Specification: interpreting a general word to exclude some of its individuals.
لام استغراق (lam istighraq): The definite article used to indicate generality, covering all individuals of a genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi position on the obligation of ghusl for nocturnal emission (ihtilam) when no emission is confirmed?
A) It is not obligatory because the hadith 'al-ma' min al-ma' only covers explicit emission.
B) It is obligatory because of another hadith that mentions meeting of circumcised parts, and ihtilam is included due to sexual desire.
C) It is obligatory only if the person remembers a dream and feels wetness.
D) It is not obligatory because the Ansar's argument using the lam of generality is correct.

Key Takeaway
A nass only governs its explicit case; silence is not negation, and extension requires a separate proof.

Mafhum al-Mukhalafa: The Hanafi Critique
Articulation of the usul principle that specificity of description/condition implies negation elsewhere.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Shafi'i principle of mafhum al-mukhalafa and explain why Hanafis reject it as an invalid method of inference.

Core Idea
Specific condition does not automatically negate the ruling elsewhere in Hanafi usul.

This passage introduces a core point of usul al-fiqh: when a legal ruling is tied to a specific description or condition, does it necessarily imply the opposite ruling when that condition is absent? Imam al-Shafi'i held that it does (mafhum al-mukhalafa), while the Hanafi school considers this inference invalid (fāsid) unless supported by separate evidence. Understanding this disagreement is fundamental to distinguishing between the two schools' approaches to textual interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects of the rule
Read the passage and extract the two forms: (1) ruling attached to a condition implies negation elsewhere; (2) ruling attached to a description implies negation where the description is absent.
2
Understand the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i treats this mafhum al-mukhalafa as a valid method of inference from texts like 'If you are on a journey and do not find water, perform tayammum' – implying that when not on a journey, tayammum is not permitted.
3
Recognize the Hanafi critique
The text labels this method as the 'second invalid reason' (دوسری وجہ فاسد). Hanafis argue that a condition or description does not by itself negate the ruling elsewhere; the absence of a ruling is determined by other evidence, not mere textual form.
Hanafis prioritize mafhum al-muwāfaqa (harmonious implication) over mafhum al-mukhalafa.
4
Compare with Hanafi usul practice
In Hanafi usul, the default is that commands and conditions are not automatically read as exclusive. For example, the verse 'When you stand up for prayer, wash your faces...' does not imply that prayer is invalid without ablution when the verse is read as a condition; the obligation of wudu is established by other evidence, not merely by the conditional form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله والحكم اذا اضيف الى المسنى بوصف خاص او علق بشرط الخ .
دوسری وجہ فاسد کا بیان
امام شافعی کے اس طریق استدلال کی دو شقیں ہیں (1) کسی حکم کو اگر کسی شرط کے ساتھ خاص کر دیا جائے تو وہ اپنے ماعدا میں حکم کی نفی پر دلالت کرتا ہے (۲) کسی علم کو کسی وصف کے ساتھ متصف کیا جائے تو جہاں وصف نہیں ہوگا وہاں حکم بھی نہیں پایا
He said: And when a ruling is added to a specific description or attached to a condition, etc. Statement of the second invalid reason. Imam Shafi'i's method of inference has two aspects: (1) If a ruling is specified with a condition, it indicates negation of the ruling in all other cases; (2) If a ruling is characterized with a description, then where the description is not present, the ruling is also not found.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage states a key usul principle: when a legal ruling (hukm) is attached to a specific description (wasf) or condition (shart), it necessarily implies that the ruling does not apply when that description or condition is absent. This is called mafhūm al-mukhālafa (implication of opposition) in Shafi'i usul, but Hanafis treat it as a sign of invalidity (fāsid) in reasoning unless there is additional evidence. The text presents this as the second aspect of Imam Shafi'i's argument that the Hanafis consider invalid. The student should memorize this principle as a standard usul maxim.

Key Terms
شرط (sharṭ): A condition upon which a ruling is contingent; the ruling applies only when the condition is met.
وصف (waṣf): A description or attribute accompanying a ruling; the ruling is restricted to instances where the description exists.
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhūm al-mukhālafah): The implication of opposition; inferring that the ruling is negated when a mentioned condition or description is absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this text, what is the status of the principle that a ruling attached to a condition is negated in its absence?
A) It is a sound method of inference.
B) It is an invalid (fāsid) method of inference.
C) It is only valid for worship.
D) It is accepted by all schools.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, attaching a ruling to a condition or description does not by itself negate the ruling in other cases; additional evidence is required.

Shafi'i's Istidlal on Condition and Attribute
Presents Shafi'i's two-pronged istidlal and the beginning of Hanafi critique

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Imam al-Shafi'i's two-pronged istidlal using conditions and attributes, and state the Hanafi critique regarding mafhum al-mukhālafa.

Core Idea
Shafi'i argues that specifying a ruling by condition or attribute negates it elsewhere; Hanafis reject this as a universal proof.

This lesson examines Imam al-Shafi'i's foundational argument in usul al-fiqh for mafhum al-mukhālafa. He argues that when a ruling is tied to a condition or attribute, it implies the opposite when that condition or attribute is absent. The commentator here lays out Shafi'i's two branches and begins to critique them from a Hanafi perspective. Understanding this dispute is essential for grasping the Hanafi approach to textual interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify Shafi'i's two branches
Shafi'i divides his argument into two: (1) condition implies negation when absent, (2) attribute implies negation when absent.
These are the two prongs of his istidlal.
2
Examine the condition example
In Quran 4:25, marriage to slave girls is conditioned upon inability to marry free believing women. Shafi'i argues that the condition negates permissibility for those who can marry free women.
Focus on the phrase 'مَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ'.
3
Examine the attribute example
In the same verse, slave girls are described as 'believing'. Shafi'i argues that this attribute negates permissibility for non-believing slave girls.
The phrase 'الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ' is the key attribute.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Shafi'i equates attribute with condition (ilhaq al-wasf bi al-shart), treating both as implying negation when absent.
This is the basis of his argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قونه والحكم اذا اضيف الى المسنى بوصف خاص او علق بشرط الخ .
دوسری وجہ فاسد کا بیان
امام شافعی کے اس طریق استدلال کی دو شقیں ہیں (1) کسی حکم کو اگر کسی شرط کے ساتھ خاص کر دیا جائے تو وہ اپنے ماعدا میں حکم کی نفی پر دلالت کرتا ہے (۲) کسی علم کو کسی وصف کے ساتھ متصف کیا جائے تو جہاں وصف نہیں ہوگا وہاں حکم بھی نہیں پایا جائیگا۔
(1) پہلی شق کی مثال : ۔۔۔۔ اللہ تعالی نے فرمایا ہے ومن لم يستطع منكم طولاً ان ينكح المحصنات المؤمنات فمن ما ملكت ايمانكم (القرآن) طرز استدلال
اللہ تعالی نے باندیوں کے ساتھ نکاح کو عدم طول حرہ کی شرط کے ساتھ مشروط کیا ہے۔ لہذا جہاں یہ شرط نہ پائی جائے یعنی جو شخص مومن آزاد عورت سے نکاح کرنے پر قدرت رکھتا ہو اس کے لئے باندیوں سے نکاح جائز نہیں (۲) دوسری شق کی مثال :
آیت میں ای آیت میں اللہ تعالی نے باندیوں کو مؤمنات کی صفت کے ساتھ متصف فرمایا ہے: قال تعالى فمن ما ملكت ايمانكم من فتياتكم المؤمنات لهذا وصف ماعدا سے حکم کی نفی پر دلالت کرے گا۔ یعنی اہل کتاب کی باندیوں سے نکاح جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
وحاصله الأول انه الحق بالشرط و الثاني : منبر الخ. ماتن رحمتہ اللہ نے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جائزہ لیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ امام شافعی کی دلیل کی بنیاد دو چیزوں پر ہے جن کا بیان مندرجہ ذیل ہے
(۱) وصف کا شرط کے ساتھ الحاق:
امام شافعی کا خیال یہ ہے کہ جس طرح شرط کے وجود پر حکم کے وجود کا اور اس کے عدم پر حکم کے عدم کا دارو مدار ہے ( اذا وجد الشرط وجد الحكم والا فلا ) اسی طرح وصف کا معاملہ بھی ہے۔ الغرض کسی نے اپنی بیوی کو یوں طلاق دی انت طالق راكبة تو ان کے ہاں طلاق اس کے رکوب کے ساتھ معلق ہوگی جس طرح اس قول میں ہے انت طالق ان كنت
His saying: 'And the ruling, when attributed to something by a specific attribute or attached to a condition, etc.' The statement of the second invalid reason. Imam Shafi'i's method of istidlal (deduction) has two branches: (1) If a ruling is specified by a condition, it indicates the negation of the ruling in other than that condition. (2) If a ruling is described with an attribute, then where the attribute is not found, the ruling is also not found. (1) Example of the first branch: Allah Most High says: 'And whoever among you does not have the means to marry free believing women, then [marry] those of your right hands...' (Quran). Method of deduction: Allah made marriage to slave girls conditional on the inability to marry free women. Therefore, where this condition is not found—i.e., a person who has the ability to marry a free believing woman—marriage to slave girls is not permissible. (2) Example of the second branch: In the verse, Allah described slave girls with the attribute of 'believing': He said: '...of your believing slave girls.' So this attribute will indicate the negation of the ruling from other than that attribute. That is, marriage to slave girls from the People of the Book is not permissible. And the summary of the first is that he attached [the ruling] to the condition, and the second: [he attached it] to an attribute, etc. The author (matan), may Allah have mercy on him, analyzing the argument of Imam Shafi'i, said that Imam Shafi'i's argument is based on two things, the explanation of which is as follows: (1) Annexation of the attribute to the condition: Imam Shafi'i is of the view that just as the existence of the ruling depends on the existence of the condition and the non-existence of the ruling on the non-existence of the condition (if the condition exists, the ruling exists, otherwise not), similarly is the case with the attribute. In short, if a man divorces his wife by saying, 'You are divorced if you are riding,' then according to them the divorce will be suspended upon her riding, just like in the statement: 'You are divorced if you are...'
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Shafi'i's argument in usul al-fiqh regarding mafhum al-mukhālafa (opposite implication). Shafi'i holds that when a ruling is attached to a condition or described by an attribute, that implies the ruling is negated when the condition or attribute is absent. The commentator (sharh) here is explaining the matn (Noor al-Anwar) which critiques this argument. The passage provides two examples from the Quran: (1) The verse permitting marriage to slave girls is conditioned upon inability to marry free women; Shafi'i argues that if one can marry a free woman, marrying a slave girl is forbidden. (2) The same verse describes the slave girls as 'believing'; Shafi'i argues this attribute excludes non-believing slave girls, so marrying a kitabi slave girl is impermissible. The matn (author of Noor al-Anwar) then analyzes Shafi'i's reasoning, stating that it consists of annexing the attribute to the condition (i.e., treating them alike). The example of conditional divorce ('You are divorced if you are riding') illustrates that for Shafi'i, an attribute (riding) functions like a condition. The passage cuts off before completing the Hanafi critique, but the intent is to show the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is over mafhum al-mukhālafa: Hanafis generally do not accept it as a decisive proof.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhālafa): The opposite implication: that specifying a condition/attribute negates the ruling otherwise
الحاق الوصف بالشرط (ilhaq al-wasf bi al-shart): Annexing the attribute to the condition, i.e., treating them equally in implying negation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Shafi'i, what does the attribute 'believing' in the verse about slave girls imply?
A) The attribute is only for praise, no legal effect
B) Marrying non-believing slave girls is impermissible
C) All slave girls are permissible to marry
D) The attribute is irrelevant

Key Takeaway
Shafi'i's argument that conditions and attributes imply negation in their absence is a key point of ikhtilaf with Hanafis, who require additional evidence for negation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
9 min
Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Mutlaq and Muqayyad in Kafarat
Dispute on carrying absolute to restricted in expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi critique of the Shafi'i principle that the absolute is carried to the restricted in expiations and identify the key methodological differences between the schools.

Core Idea
Non-existence is not a Shari ruling; each expiation has its own specific text.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is over whether an absolute (mutlaq) term in one expiation must be restricted by a qualified (muqayyad) term in another expiation when the legal causes appear similar. The Shafi'is argue for extension based on a principle about conditional sentences and the unity of expiations, while the Hanafis reject this, emphasizing that non-existence (adam) is not a transposable ruling and that expiations differ in severity. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate qiyas and apply Hanafi usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i principle
Extract the Shafi'i rule: 'When the condition or description is absent, the ruling is absent.' Note that they treat non-payment as a Shari ruling.
This principle is used to argue that the absence of faith in a slave leads to the absence of expiation payment.
2
Understand the Shafi'i application to expiations
See how the Shafi'is apply this: in murder expiation (freeing a believing slave), they derive two rulings (payment with believing slave, non-payment with unbelieving slave) and extend the restriction of faith to all expiations via qiyas, claiming unity of expiations.
They rely on the idea that all expiations share the same underlying cause.
3
Analyze the Hanafi critique
Identify the Hanafi response: the only Shari ruling is the positive one; non-payment is original non-existence (adam asli), not a ruling that can be extended. Also, expiations are not identical – murder is graver.
Hanafis distinguish between absence of a condition and a positive ruling about that absence.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi counter-objection
Follow the objection: if Shafi'is extend the believing slave condition to oath expiation, they should also extend feeding sixty poor from zihar to murder expiation. The Hanafi response: a proper noun (ism 'alam) establishes distinction, and feeding is not specified in murder.
This shows the Hanafi insistence on textual specificity over analogical extension.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: in zihar expiation, Shafi'is require a believing slave; Hanafis accept any slave. Also, in oath expiation, Hanafis accept clothing as alternative; Shafi'is would require a believing slave if they extend.
The dispute directly affects what a mukallaf must do in expiation.

Source Text

قوله وقد يقدر الاختلاف بيننا وبينه الخ
حضرت مولانا شیخ احمد جیون فرماتے ہیں کہ اسی اختلاف کو ایک دوسرے انداز سے بھی بیان کیا جاتا ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ شوافع کے ہاں مذکورہ تمام کلام جملہ شرطیہ ہے اور جملہ شرطیہ میں حکم صرف جزا میں ہوتا ہے جبکہ شرط کی حیثیت ظرف یا حال کی ہے۔ اس مذھب کو عرب اہل لسان کی طرف بھی منسوب کیا گیا ہے۔ جو محض افتراء ہے بلکہ ان کے ہاں چونکہ جملہ شرطیہ شرط اور جزاء دونوں کے مجموعے کا نام ہے لہذا حکم بھی شرط اور جزاء دونوں کے درمیان ہوتا ہے۔ اور مذکور مذهب صرف صاحب مفتاح کا ہے۔
تیسری وجہ فاسد کا بیان
والمطلق محمول على المقيد الخ: امام شافعی کی اس دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مسئلہ شرعیہ میں مطلق اور مقید حکم مذکور ہوں تو مطلق کو مقید کے تابع کر کے مقید والی قید اس میں بھی ثابت کی جائے گی مثلاً کفارہ ظہار میں تین حکم ہیں۔ اور تیرا حکم یعنی اطعام ستين مسكيناً من قبل ان يتماسا کی قید کے ساتھ مقید نہیں مگر ان کے ہاں ضروری ہے کہ مظاہر اطعام کی تکمیل تک بھی جماع نہ کرے ورنہ امادہ واجب ہوتا ۔ یہاں حادثہ متحد ہے اور وہ ہے کفارہ قتل کی طرح ان کے ہاں دیگر تمام کفاروں میں بھی مؤمن غلام آزاد کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ کیونکہ تمام کفارے کفارہ ہونے میں برابر ہیں ۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل:
ان کا ایک اصول ہے کہ اذا انتفى الشرط او الوصف انتفى الحكم ۔ اور طریق استدلال یہ ہے کہ ان کے ہاں مخصوص یعنی کفارہ قتل فتحرير رقبة مؤمنة میں دو حکم ہیں (۱) رقبه مؤمنہ سے ادائیگی کفارہ اور (۲) رقبة غير مؤمنہ سے عدم ادائیگی اور دونوں حکم شرعی ہیں لہذا اتحاد کفارات کے باعث قیاس کا تقاضا ہے کہ ان کو وہ سرے کفارات کی طرف متعدی کیا جائے ۔ بعض شوافع قیاس کی بھی شرط لگاتے ہیں۔
احناف کا جواب اور موقف :
حکم شرعی تو صرف رقبہ مؤمنہ سے ادائیگی کفارہ ہے رہی عدم ادائیگی تو وہ عدم اصلی ہے اور عدم متعدی نہیں ہوتا ۔ نیز کفارے سب ایک جیسے بھی نہیں بلکہ قتل کا جرم اغلط ہے لہذا انصاف کا تقاضا ہے کہ سزا بھی اسی کے مناسب ہو لہذا غلام کے ساتھ ایمان کی قید لگادی جبکہ دیگر جرائم اس درجہ کے نہیں، لہذا قید لگانا ظلم ہے
:قوله ثم اعترض على الشافعى رحمه الله انكم كما حملتم اليمين الخ
اعتراض:
شوافع نے جس طرح اتحاد کفارہ کی بنیاد پر کفارہ قتل پر کفارہ یمین کو محمول کر کے اسمیں بھی رقبہ کے لئے ایمان کی قید ثابت کی ہے اسی طرح انہیں چاہیے کہ کفارہ یمین پر کفارہ قتل کو اطعام مساکین کے حق میں محمول کریں۔
جواب:
اسم علم سے تفاوت ثابت ہے اور یمین میں طعام منصوص ہے اور قتل میں اصل طعام ہی منصوص نہیں۔ اور اہم علم سے وجود تو ثابت ہوتا ہے لیکن وہ اپنے عدم کے وقت عدم حکم کو ثابت نہیں کرتا ۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اسم علم اصل یعنی کفارہ یمین میں بھی عدم اطعام کی صورت میں ادائے کفارہ کی نفی نہیں بلکہ کسوہ بھی کافی ہے۔ تو فرع (قتل) میں حکم کیسے متعدی ہوگا۔
قوله وانما قيد الطعام باليمين الخ
شارخ العلام رحمۃ اللہ علیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے اعتراض کفارہ یمین کو لیکر کیا ہے کیونکہ امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ کی ایک روایت میں کفارہ ظہار یعنی ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھانا کھا نا کفارہ قتل میں بھی ثابت ہے
He said: And the difference between us and him may be estimated, etc. Hadhrat Maulana Sheikh Ahmad Jiyun says that this difference is also explained in another way, the summary of which is that according to the Shafi'is, all the aforementioned speech is a conditional sentence, and in a conditional sentence the ruling is only in the consequence, while the condition is like a circumstance or state. This opinion has also been attributed to the Arab linguists, which is pure slander. Rather, according to them, since the conditional sentence is the name for the combination of both condition and consequence, the ruling also occurs between both condition and consequence. And this opinion is only that of the author of al-Miftah. The third invalid reason: 'And the absolute is carried on the restricted, etc.': The summary of Imam Shafi'i's proof is that if in a Shar'i issue both absolute and restricted rulings are mentioned, then the absolute is subordinated to the restricted and the restriction mentioned therein is also established. For example, in the expiation of zihar, there are three rulings. And the third ruling, i.e., feeding sixty poor before touching, is not restricted with a condition, but according to them it is necessary that the muzahir does not have intercourse until the completion of feeding, otherwise [something] becomes wajib. Here the incident is the same, and it is like the expiation of murder; according to them, in all other expiations it is necessary to free a believing slave, because all expiations are equal in being expiation. Imam Shafi'i's proof: They have a principle: 'When the condition or description is absent, the ruling is absent.' And the way of derivation is that according to them, the specific case, i.e., the expiation of murder, 'then free a believing slave' has two rulings: (1) paying expiation by a believing slave, and (2) non-payment by a non-believing slave. And both rulings are Shari' rulings. Therefore, due to the unity of expiations, qiyas requires that they be transposed to all expiations. Some Shafi'is also stipulate qiyas. The Hanafis' answer and stance: The Shari' ruling is only the payment of expiation by a believing slave; as for non-payment, it is original non-existence, and non-existence is not transposable. Also, expiations are not all the same; rather, murder is a greater crime, so justice requires that the punishment be proportionate. Therefore, the restriction of faith was placed on the slave, while other crimes are not of this level, so imposing a restriction is injustice. Then he said: He objected to al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him: 'Just as you carried the oath, etc.' Objection: Just as the Shafi'is, on the basis of the unity of expiation, carried the expiation of oath upon the expiation of murder and established therein the restriction of faith for the slave, similarly they should carry the expiation of murder upon the expiation of oath with respect to feeding the poor. Answer: A proper noun establishes distinction, and in the oath, feeding is specified, while in murder, feeding is not specified at all. And a proper noun establishes existence, but it does not establish the negation of a ruling at the time of its non-existence. The gist of the answer is that in the original, i.e., the expiation of oath, even in the case of not feeding, the payment of expiation is not negated; rather, clothing is also sufficient. So how can the ruling be transposed to the branch (murder)? He said: 'And the food was only restricted with the oath, etc.' The commentator, may Allah's mercy be upon him, says: We have made the objection regarding the expiation of oath because in one narration of Imam Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, the expiation of zihar, i.e., feeding sixty poor, is also established in the expiation of murder.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and the Shafi'is regarding the principle of carrying the absolute (mutlaq) to the restricted (muqayyad), specifically in the context of expiations (kafarat). The author begins by noting an alternative expression of the dispute: the Shafi'is treat the entire statement as a conditional sentence, with the ruling only in the consequence, but this is refuted by noting that the conditional sentence includes both condition and consequence, so the ruling encompasses both. Then the third invalid reason of the Shafi'is is discussed: the principle 'and the absolute is carried on the restricted' is applied to expiations. Imam Shafi'i argues that if an absolute and a restricted ruling occur, the absolute must be subordinated to the restricted. For example, in zihar expiation, feeding sixty poor is absolute, but by analogy to murder expiation, it should be restricted by 'before touching'. This is based on the unity of expiations (ittihad al-kafarat) — all expiations are similar, so a believing slave is required in all. The Shafi'i proof is their principle: 'When the condition or description is absent, the ruling is absent.' They claim that in the verse for murder expiation (Quran 4:92: 'freeing a believing slave'), there are two Shari rulings: payment with a believing slave and non-payment with an unbelieving slave. This non-payment is also a Shari ruling, so by qiyas it extends to all expiations. The Hanafi response is that the Shari ruling is only the positive payment; non-payment is original non-existence (adam asli), which is not transposable. Moreover, expiations are not all equal; murder is a greater crime, so its punishment is stricter (requiring faith in the slave), while other crimes are lesser, so imposing faith would be unjust. The Hanafis then raise an objection: If the Shafi'is carry the oath expiation (kafarat al-yamin) onto murder expiation to require a believing slave, then by the same logic, they should carry murder expiation onto oath expiation to require feeding the poor. The response is that the proper noun (ism 'alam) establishes distinction: in oath expiation, feeding is explicitly specified (mansus), while in murder expiation, feeding is not specified at all. Furthermore, the proper noun establishes existence but does not establish the negation of a ruling in its absence — in oath expiation, if one cannot feed, clothing suffices, so the ruling is not negated. Thus, the transposition to murder fails. The commentator clarifies that the objection specifically targets Shafi'i's narration equating zihar expiation with murder expiation. This passage exemplifies the Hanafi approach of restricting analogies to specific texts and not extending them arbitrarily, highlighting their reliance on istihsan (juristic preference) and attention to differences in underlying causes (illah).

Key Terms
مطلق (mutlaq): An unqualified term without any condition or restriction, applied to its subject without any additional qualification.
مقيد (muqayyad): A term qualified by a condition, description, or other restriction that limits its application.
كفارة (kafarah): Expiatory act prescribed for certain sins or omissions, such as breaking an oath, zihar, or accidental killing.
اتحاد (ittihad): Unity or identity of legal cause, which the Shafi'is argue makes qiyas between different expiations valid.
عدم (adam): Non-existence; here used in the sense of original non-existence (adam asli) as opposed to a Shari ruling of negation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis in this passage, why is the non-payment of expiation with a non-believing slave not a valid Shari ruling that can be extended to other expiations?
A) Because the Shafi'is only claimed it, but it has no textual basis.
B) Because it is original non-existence (adam asli), not a positive ruling.
C) Because the non-believing slave is not mentioned in the Quran at all.
D) Because qiyas is not allowed in matters of expiation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis hold that the absolute is not automatically restricted in expiations because non-existence is not a transposable Shari ruling, and each expiation has its own specific legal cause.
